Qian Da, a Partner at a Stove Shop in Pudong, Electrocuted to Death During Thunderstorm Yesterday Afternoon 107

Yesterday afternoon, dark clouds gathered in the sky, and heavy rain poured down. At about 2:00 p.m., thunder and lightning struck, deafening. At that time, Qian Da (32 years old), a partner from Rufou, was working at a stove shop in a shed behind Tongchunfu in Laobaibo, Pudong. Because it was raining heavily and no one was fetching water, he was mixing water in the various water pots with a water ladle when suddenly a thunderbolt struck, electrocuting Qian Da and killing him. He fell inside the door, with his head to the north and feet to the south, and no breath left. Yang Zhongquan, the head of the Yangjiabo Police Station, heard the report and sent police officers to investigate. They saw that the deceased was bare-chested and wearing shorts. His skin had not changed color. It was learned that the owner of the shop had returned to his hometown and had not returned. Zhu Henian is currently managing the shop. The deceased has no relatives in Shanghai. The police station head has instructed the local baojia, Yang Baobao, to report to the local court and request an autopsy for the purpose of collecting the body for burial.

The Taxpayers' Association Will Again Write to Request Correction: Chaotic Telephone Accounts and a List of Various Malpractices and Errors 108

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession, yesterday sent a letter to the Public Works Department (工部局), which read: "Sir, according to a letter from the Shijin Taiji Printing Bureau (時進泰記印務局), we received a warning letter from the telephone company stating that the telephone bill in question must be paid immediately, otherwise the line would be cut. Upon reading this, we were extremely surprised. We immediately sent a letter on the 17th stating that we had a receipt as proof. The telephone bill is paid within ten days of receiving the bill, and we have a receipt as proof. Such errors have occurred several times before, including listing paid bills on the statement without noticing. What is the basis for this warning letter? On the morning of the 20th, the line was cut. The company should be fully responsible for the loss of reputation and business suffered by our firm. We are sending a copy of the company's receipt from August to the 26th of this month. Please examine it and arrange for negotiations to seek justice for our unwarranted losses."

The association also stated that the accounts of the Shanghai Telephone Company are extremely chaotic. The association receives reports about this almost daily, and it is common knowledge that overcharging and double-charging are frequent occurrences, while some go without payment for six months to a year. There have already been one or two such reports. For those who have paid but have their lines cut, such losses are difficult for users to calculate. It is even stranger that some can continue to talk for months without paying, which increases the burden on other responsible users. Even stranger, some continue to receive monthly bills for months after their lines have been cut. Such bad debts are passed on to other responsible users through price increases. The company's chaotic accounts also mean that there are many unnecessary losses in management. The bureau should promptly exercise its supervisory powers to correct the company's major errors. After reading the attached documents, please return them immediately. Sincerely, to Mr. Fei, Acting Director-General of the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department."

North Station Loading and Unloading Workers: Old and New Workers Brawl, Railway Bureau Cancels Cooperative, Sends Personnel to Reorganize, More Than Twenty People Injured in the Fight for Work 109

Loading and unloading workers at the North Station of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, new and old workers fought over work yesterday morning, leaving many injured. The following is a detailed report from a reporter of the Xin Sheng She (新聲社).

Personnel Sent to Reorganize: There are more than 130 official loading and unloading workers at the North Station. In the past, the workers formed the "Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway North Station Loading and Unloading Workers Cooperative," led by Gao Ge (高閣) and Cui Shitai (崔士太). These people were arrested and detained by the Garrison Headquarters on suspicion of being Communists. The Railway Bureau recently announced the cancellation of the cooperative on the 23rd because of poor management and sent Sun Zhusan (孫祝三) to reorganize it. The workers expressed their support for Sun's reorganization but strongly opposed the new workers taking over the work.

Section Chief's Announcement: A notice from the Su-Song Section of the Traffic Department stated, "Regarding the announcement, we have received an order from the Traffic Department stating that the loading and unloading workers' cooperative at the North Station is poorly managed and should be canceled immediately. With the approval of the Administration Bureau, Sun Zhusan is ordered to reorganize it within a specified period. During the reorganization, the Section Chief should pay close attention to all relevant accounts of the cooperative and clearly delineate them. In addition to notifying the police to assist, we urgently request the Section Chief to handle the matter carefully." The notice was issued by Section Chief Wang Shuchun (王樹春).

Old and New Fight: At 8:00 AM yesterday morning, Sun Zhusan, the contractor, led more than ten new workers to the freight yard at No. 5 Jiaotong Road to prepare for takeover. The old workers sent representatives Wei Yue (韋約) and Meng Hongyun (孟洪雲) to negotiate with Sun Zhusan. Immediately, the new workers and more than 100 temporary workers outside the gate started fighting with the old workers. (In the past, when work was busy, temporary workers were hired to help in addition to the original workers, but in recent years, business has been slow, and temporary workers have no work to do, so disputes have often arisen.) A large number of military police were dispatched by the 9th Platoon of the 3rd Battalion of the 1st Regiment of the Security Team of the 2nd Precinct of the 5th District of the Public Security Bureau and the police departments of both roads to suppress the violence, but they were ineffective.

List of Injured: As a result of the fighting, the following old workers were injured: (1) Liu Zhuanliang (劉專良), injured in the back; (2) Liu Dexing (劉德興), injured in the waist; (3) Xu Bulan (許步蘭), injured in the head; (4) Guo Xingru (郭興如), injured in the head; (5) Ding Wanshan (丁萬山), injured in the head; (6) Yang Ruqi (楊如其), injured in the face; (7) Jin Wanfu (金完福), injured in the waist. These seven people were bandaged at the Pazit Railway Hospital and then discharged. (8) Guo Shunfu (郭順甫), injured in the chest, remains hospitalized. (9) Xiao Sizi (小四子), injured in the eye; (10) Zhang Guangfu (張光甫), injured in the head; (11) Shi Gaoxiang (史高祥), injured in the face; (12) Substitute worker Yang Xiaoma Zhi (楊小麻支), injured in the head. The following new and temporary workers were injured: (1) Wang Jiaqing (王家慶), thirty holes in the head; (2) Bao Konghua (包孔華), internal injuries, bandaged and discharged from the Haig Road Red Cross Hospital; (3) Chang Jinshan (常金山), injured in the waist; (4) Wu Changsheng (吳長生), injured in the back; (5) Hu Yuebang (胡月邦), injured in the waist, hospitalized at Renji Hospital; (6) Ding Sugeng (丁素耕), injured in the head; (7) Xu Desheng (許德生), injured in the face; (8) Xi Qiaosen (奚巧森), injured in the shoulder; (9) Cao Guanggui (曹光桂), injured in the head; (10) Yuan Jintang (願金堂), injured in the hand; (11) Xie Chenggong (謝成功), injured in the hand; (12) Jin Bingtang (金炳堂), injured in the face; (13) Zhao Guangzhi (趙光志). The last two are hospitalized at Tongren Hospital.

Workers Detained: The Public Security Bureau of the 2nd Precinct of the 5th District detained the following workers from both sides who committed the violence: Meng Hongqi (孟洪其), Shi Gaoxiang (史高祥), Zhang Guangfu (張光甫), Yang Maosong (楊茂松), Wang Jiaqing (王家慶), Bao Zhahua (包扎華), Chang Jinshan (常金山), Wu Changsheng (吳長生), Xia Renchu (夏仁初), Yuan Jintang (願金堂), Zhu Dexi (朱德喜), Shi Jiezhi (石潔芝), Zhou Muyi (周慕頥), Pan Hanchen (潘涵臣), Wang Changhai (王長海), Li Defu (李德富), Tang Zhirong (唐志榮), Liu Chaoshan (劉朝山), Jin Bingfa (金炳發), Cao Guangrong (曹光榮), Zhang Kaitong (張凱通), Zhang Guangjin (張光金), Yang Shende (楊愼德), Yang Ruhe (楊如恒), Wang Hongzhang (王鴻章), Huang Yangai (黄揚藹), Li Yuzhu (李玉珠), Sun Zhizhi (孫　之), and more than 20 others, as well as those who came with Sun Zhu'er. They were all taken to the station for questioning. After Police Chief Chen Jiwu (陳繼武) failed to persuade them to stop, they were sent to the bureau at 6:00 PM.

Railway Bureau Investigates: All loading and unloading workers continue to load and unload goods as usual. A reporter from Xin Sheng She learned from the Railway Bureau yesterday that the bureau, in view of the North Station Loading and Unloading Workers Cooperative's inability to effectively manage the loading and unloading at the North Station, specially sent Sun San to reorganize it. Since the conflict occurred yesterday morning, the Traffic Department has sent officials from Nanjing to thoroughly investigate the matter and report to the bureau chief for review. It is believed that Sun Zhusan is a reorganization officer, and if the cooperative refuses to reorganize, it can be reported to the Railway Bureau for review. There should be no conflict with the cooperative. A fair disposition will be made after the investigation.

Party Headquarters' Response: The reporter also went to the Party Headquarters of both roads. A member of the committee informed us that the Railway Bureau's appointment of personnel to reorganize the cooperative was not known to the headquarters beforehand. After the incident, the truth was investigated separately and can be divided into three points: (1) The cause was purely a struggle for livelihood. The conflict between long-term workers and temporary workers arose from this. To avoid conflicts, the problem of workers' livelihoods must be solved. (2) Responsibility: Sun Zhusan was ordered to reorganize and should not have led new workers to compete for work. Therefore, Sun should bear full responsibility. (3) Aftermath: The Party Headquarters decided to deal with the matter in a reasonable and fair manner and has already reported the matter to the central government for instructions and a decision.

Sun Zhusan's Account: Sun Zhusan said that he was ordered by the Traffic Department to take over the loading and unloading work at the North Freight Yard on the 24th. To prevent misunderstandings, he repeatedly persuaded the workers on the 24th and 25th. At 8:00 AM on the 26th, he went to the yard again to prepare for the takeover. As he was talking to the workers' representatives Zhang Yue and Meng Hongyun, a martial drama suddenly broke out outside the yard. The yard immediately closed all the doors. Not long after, the long-term workers broke down the doors and entered the station chief's writing room, making things difficult for him. Fortunately, military police suppressed the violence, avoiding a major disaster. He only brought eleven or twelve people to the yard. He knew nothing about the fighting outside the yard beforehand. Finally, a large number of police officers from the Yongxing Road Police Station escorted him and the others to the police station. According to various statements, the two sides were still the past temporary workers and official workers fighting over work. The long-term workers believed that the fighting was caused by Sun. However, the results of the injuries on both sides showed that there were more than ten temporary workers injured, while only five or six long-term workers were injured. Sun immediately sent a letter from Xiao, director of the Traffic Department, to the Public Security Bureau to prove that he did not instigate the violence.

Railway Bureau's News: According to news from the Railway Bureau yesterday, the original workers and temporary workers in the Loading and Unloading Cooperative at the North Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway were divided into two factions, who were hostile to each other and often had disputes. The cooperative's chief foreman, Gao Ge, and the temporary workers' leader, Liu, had no control over the situation. Recently, the Railway Bureau feared that their disputes would escalate and cause an accident. It approved the request of a third party, Sun Zhusan, to try to take responsibility for the reorganization. Just as he was about to begin, yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, the two factions of the original workers had another misunderstanding over a minor matter and started fighting on Jiaotong Road. Fortunately, it was quickly quelled. Several people on both sides were injured, but none were serious. After someone is responsible for the reorganization, the aforementioned accidents may no longer occur. It is heard that the Railway Bureau has dispatched Jiang Nan to investigate.

HUA FENG Flour Factory Workers Clash with Detectives Yesterday, Worker Liu Mingwu Injured and Life-Threatening, Western Detective Also Slightly Injured, Two Workers Arrested 110

More than 300 workers at the Huafeng Xingji Flour Factory (華豐興記　粉廠) on Xiaoshadu Road (小沙渡路) went to the home of the factory representative, Ye Shantao (葉山濤), in Zundeli (尊德里), Xiamen Road (厦門路) to petition for the resumption of work and the maintenance of food expenses. Because they did not get what they wanted, they did not disperse until yesterday (24th). The Laozha (老閘) Police Station sent a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to the scene to expel them, resulting in a conflict. The details are as follows:

Detectives Sent to Expel: More than 300 workers at the Huafeng Xingji Flour Factory went to the home of the factory representative, Ye Shantao, at No. 47, Lane 5, Zundeli, Xiamen Road, at 9:00 AM on the 24th to petition for the resumption of work and the maintenance of food expenses. As a result, they did not get what they wanted, and they all slept in the lane until yesterday, refusing to leave. They ate pancakes for their meals. Yesterday afternoon at about 1:00 PM, a heavy rainstorm occurred, and the workers had no choice but to go to Ye Shantao's house to take shelter. Ye saw this situation and reported it to the Laozha Police Station, which sent more than 30 Chinese and Western detectives to the scene to expel them.

Conflict Erupts: The Laozha Police Station believed that the matter belonged to a labor strike. In order to avoid the situation from growing, it had sent more than ten Chinese and Western detectives to Zundeli to patrol in shifts, so the order was good and no incidents occurred. Until yesterday, it was reported that the workers were cooking in the lane, which could be dangerous, and they were asked to expel them. The police station sent more than 30 Chinese and Western detectives to the scene at 3:00 PM yesterday. However, the workers were determined not to leave because they were forced by livelihood and expressed that they would not give up until they achieved their goals, resulting in a conflict.

Injured and Arrested: The order was greatly disrupted at that time, and the intersection on Xiamen Road was blocked. As a result, one worker, Liu Mingwu (劉明武), was injured and was immediately taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is heard that the injury was to a vital part of the body and that his life was in danger. On the detective side, one Western head detective was also slightly injured in the head. Two workers were arrested on the spot and detained at the Laozha Police Station. The rest of the workers were completely dispersed after 2:00 PM. It is heard that the Party and government organs and the Municipal General Labor Union, considering the seriousness of the case, are actively trying to mediate in order to resolve the dispute.

Husband Abuses and Abandons, Woman Deceived into Remarriage, Woman's Circumstances Excusable, Matchmaker Cannot Be Pardoned by Law 111

Zhu Acheng (朱　成), a native of Ningbo and eleven years old, lives at No. 12, Lane　, where he works as a Western food server in a foreign firm. In February of last year, he married a woman from the same hometown, Zhou Gendi (周根弟). After the marriage, their feelings were not harmonious, and Zhu often abused Zhou. Zhou had reported this to the neighborhood, but it was not accepted on the grounds of being a family dispute. Recently, Zhu has become even more abusive, not returning home for more than a month and not providing living expenses, causing the woman to go without food for two days. In addition, she is seven months pregnant. On the 15th of this month, she was crying on the road and was seen by Miao Zhangshi (妙張氏), a native of Nanjing, who took her to the home of Sun Baoshi (孫鮑氏) and Hao Xueshi (郝薛氏) at No. 6, Lane, Tangshan Road (塘山路). Seeing that Zhu abused her so much, they suggested that she find another way to make a living. Zhou, young and ignorant, agreed. Then, Sun Baoshi and others asked a man named Wei Si (魏四) to act as a matchmaker and promised Zhou to Pu Guixiang (蒲貴相), a native of Jiangbei, as his wife. At that time, it was stated that the betrothal gift was 30 yuan, and all the miscellaneous expenses totaled 120 yuan, all of which were given to Wei Si. Pu and Zhou began living together on the 21st of the month at No. 551, Tangshan Road. However, Wei Si disappeared after receiving 120 yuan, pocketing all the money and not dividing it with Sun Baoshi and others, causing Sun Baoshi and Miao Zhangshi to think of exposing the matter. They reported to Zhu Acheng the other day. Zhu reported to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered detectives Cai Liu (蔡流), Chinese detectives Yue Ma Wenda (馬文達), and others to go and arrest Zhou Gendi, Pu Guixiang, Miao Zhangshi, and Hao Xueshi. It was found that Sun Baoshi was also involved and was detained. At that time, Sun tried to bribe the detective with two yuan, but was refused. Yesterday morning, they were taken to the 5th Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police Lawyer Li Zhishan (厲志山) explained the situation and filed a lawsuit against Zhu Zhou, and Pu Guixiang according to Article 239 of the Criminal Law, and against Sun Baoshi, Miao Zhangshi, and Hao Xueshi according to Article 231 of the Criminal Law. According to the same law, Article 122, Section 3, Sun Baoshi was also charged. After Judge Rong Duo (榮鐸) questioned each defendant one by one, the defendants all admitted to the above facts. Police Lawyer Li pleaded that Zhu Zhou's crime was due to her husband's abuse, and that she was fooled by others due to her ignorance, which was excusable. He requested that the law be applied fairly. It was obvious that Pu Guixiang saw that Zhu Zhou was pregnant and was a married woman, so he requested that the law punish him. The crimes of the remaining three defendants have been proven, so please punish them severely. The court reviewed the case and ordered a sentence to be announced at a later date. Pu Guixiang was allowed bail of 100 yuan.

Verdict in the Yong'an Silver Company Case: Ou Jiancheng Sentenced to One Year in Prison for Both Crimes, Lin Kanghou Fined 200 Yuan for Violating Registration Regulations 112

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xiefen (蕭爕棻) of the First Special District Court opened the Third Court to announce the verdict in the Yong'an Silver Company bankruptcy case, which had been in litigation for more than half a year. The main text stated that Ou Jiancheng (歐建成) was found guilty of jointly and continuously defrauding property and sentenced to ten months of imprisonment. He was also found guilty of embezzlement and sentenced to six months of imprisonment, to be served concurrently for a total of one year. Lin Kanghou (林康侯) was found guilty of jointly violating the provisions of the Company Law regarding the time limit for applying for registration and was fined 200 yuan, which could be commuted to labor service at the rate of two yuan per day. Luo Huafang (羅華舫) was acquitted. The portion of the case involving Cao Shuzhen (曹淑貞) was not accepted. The defendants Ou Jiancheng and Lin Kanghou should jointly and severally compensate Zhang Jinshui (張金水) 556.86 yuan and Cao Zhushi (曹朱氏) 500 yuan. Ou Jiancheng should compensate Liu Jialin (劉家林) 1717.77 yuan, all with interest calculated from the date of deposit until the date of execution. The lawsuit of the plaintiff Cao Shuzhen and the incidental civil lawsuits of Cao Zhushi and Xie Zhongying (謝仲英) were transferred to the Civil Court of this court for trial. It is heard that the court has now scheduled a hearing for the remaining responsible persons of the company, such as Deng Jinghuan (鄧鏡寰), on the afternoon of September 25.

Dispute Over Real Estate Mortgage Agency Rights: Zhang Danru Sues, Stock Exchange Refuses to Acknowledge, Court Orders Further Investigation and Resumes Hearing 113

Moli Shi (莫理十) and others, members of the estate management committee of British citizen Leishide (雷士德), alleged that Zhang Danru (張澹如), formerly entrusted by the Shanghai Securities and Commodities Exchange (上海證券物品交易所) as a representative and guaranteed by Xue Zhusun (薛竹蓀), mortgaged six English registered title deeds of the exchange for more than 2.8 million national currency, but neither redeemed them nor paid interest. Therefore, they hired lawyer Xu Shihao (徐士浩) to file a lawsuit against Xue and Zhang. When the First Special District Court opened the court, the exchange sent a lawyer to deny that Zhang Danru had the right to represent the exchange in the mortgage increase in September of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). Zhang, on the other hand, claimed that he had the right to represent the exchange in all mortgages. Therefore, Zhang hired lawyer Wu Zhengxue (吳正矱) to file a lawsuit against the Shanghai Securities and Commodities Exchange to confirm his agency rights. Yesterday morning, Judge Mo Runhua (莫潤華) of the First Special District Court opened the court to hear the case. First, Wu Zhengxue, the plaintiff's agent, stated the purpose of the lawsuit, saying that in the 13th year of the Republic (1924), the exchange entrusted the plaintiff Zhang Danru to mortgage five English registered title deeds, totaling more than ten mu of land, to Englishman Leishide for 400,000 taels of silver. Subsequently, the redemption period was repeatedly extended and the mortgage was increased several times to 850,000 taels. Zhang obtained the exchange's letter of appointment as representative for the mortgage in the 18th year of the Republic (1929). Later, the exchange wanted to buy the neighboring land belonging to the English Registered No. 17, and the owner was surnamed Chen. Fearing that Chen would store goods, they asked Zhang Danru to instruct others to come forward and buy the land, which was sold for more than 10,000 taels of silver. It was then mortgaged to the Zhenye Banking Group for more than 300,000 yuan. On September 16 of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), Zhang, because the exchange's mortgage of the land to Leishide was due to be redeemed, negotiated with the Leishide Estate Management Committee to extend the term. At the same time, he still represented the company in mortgaging the title deed of No. 17, which was subject to the Zhenye Banking Group, for 450,000 yuan. However, this mortgage act was not recorded in the letter of representation that the exchange had given to the plaintiff at that time. However, the money mortgaged had been given to the exchange, and there was no objection at first. Now that the exchange suddenly raised a dispute over the limits of representation after being sued by the mortgagee, he filed a lawsuit for confirmation. The defendant, the Shanghai Securities and Commodities Exchange, through its legal representative, Yu Qiaqing (虞洽卿), the chairman of the exchange, hired lawyer Zhang Zheng (張正) to appear in court and claim that the defendant only knew that the title deed of No. 17 was mortgaged to the Zhenye Banking Group, and the 400,000 yuan mortgaged was also drawn from the group in installments. They did not entrust the plaintiff to mortgage to the Leishide Estate Management Committee, so they could not admit that he also had the right to represent the mortgage. Judge Mo ordered further investigation of the case and scheduled another hearing for a later date.

Su-Hu Highway: Lujiabang Section Destroyed 114

The Su-Hu Highway (蘇滬公路) has been selling tickets and operating since the Su-Kun section (蘇昆段) opened on the 11th of this month, which has been half a month. Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs Thoroughly Investigates the "Xu Lai Coronation Ceremony" Case, Summons Preparatory Members for Questioning 115

The Vienna Ballroom (維也納舞廳) recently held a so-called "Oriental Standard Beauty Xu Lai Coronation Ceremony." The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs believes that the name of the event is improper, the wording of its public announcement is absurd, and it is suspected of collecting money under false pretenses and obstructing public morals. At a time when the New Life Movement is being vigorously promoted, such strange phenomena should not be allowed to be promoted in Shanghai, which is related to international perception. Therefore, the bureau immediately ordered the preparatory committee to stop holding the ceremony and notified the newspapers not to publish advertisements or publicity for the coronation ceremony to avoid attracting attention. Unexpectedly, the preparatory committee dared to disregard the government order and proceeded with the ceremony as usual. Afterwards, it published a thank-you advertisement with absurd wording, almost forgetting that they were citizens of the Republic of China and must abide by Chinese laws. It is heard that the Bureau of Social Affairs will severely punish this case to deter others. It has now scheduled to summon the preparatory members Xu Shanhong (徐善宏), Shen Congshan (沈從善), etc. to the bureau for questioning and to conduct a thorough investigation.

Tobacco Exchange Industry Petitions Chamber of Commerce to Negotiate French Concession Tax Reduction Case 120

The Tobacco Exchange Industry Association of this city, regarding the French Municipal Council's increase in the tax on tobacco exchanges within the concession, was again requested yesterday by members Yingchang, Henghexing, Guangda, Qianruihe, Ruitai, Ruidayong, Xiexingtai, Yongtai, Changfeng, and other firms to petition the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for reasonable negotiations. The association then dispatched committee member Zhang Songji to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce with a document. Secretary Yan Esheng and Zhu Boyuan received him, immediately explaining the details and submitting thirty-five receipts for the increased taxes, requesting that the Chamber of Commerce provide evidence so that the increased amount could be corrected and deducted. The request was agreed to be forwarded. The original letter is recorded as follows: Respectfully, yesterday we received your association's general letter No. 3005, stating that on the 22nd of this month, we received a letter from the French Concession Municipal Council, translated as follows: "We received your association's two letters of July 25th and August 9th, stating that the tobacco exchange members of this city are experiencing operational difficulties and have no profit to gain. You have specially requested that the increase in the tobacco exchange tax be waived to alleviate the commercial burden, etc. We have reviewed and understand this. It has been verified that each tobacco exchange shop in our concession has been paying a monthly tax of 2.8 yuan. The current characteristic levy of 5.6 yuan is due to the combined collection of tobacco and exchange taxes. The amount of various taxes stipulated by our council is quite reasonable and cannot be changed at any time. We hereby respond to your inquiry." After careful consideration of the meaning of the French Concession Municipal Council's statement that "each tobacco exchange shop has been paying a monthly tax of 2.8 yuan, and the current characteristic levy of 5.6 yuan is due to the combined collection of tobacco and exchange taxes. The amount of various taxes stipulated by our council is quite reasonable and cannot be changed at any time," there is no reason for the increase in the tax. However, according to the evidence presented by the members, the tax has indeed been doubled since June. Based on the above facts, whether there was an error in the procedures of the collection personnel, we specially submit the evidence, earnestly requesting your association to examine it and promptly issue a letter to the French Concession Municipal Council to immediately correct it, in order to show compassion for the market and eliminate disputes. It is also requested that the increased amount be clarified and deducted on a monthly basis to avoid misunderstandings and alleviate the commercial burden. We are extremely grateful.

Wife Withdraws Adultery Lawsuit; Yang Gengquan Already Divorced from His Wife Out of Court 123

Yang Gengquan, a local resident and chauffeur, 34 years old this year, married a Jin woman (named Meiyu, 32 years old this year) through a matchmaker thirteen years ago. They lived together in Xiaoliang Road, Yangshupu, and had two children. Wu originally had a husband surnamed Yu, but he was weak and didn't interfere. After Yang began living with Wu, he neglected his legal wife, Jin. Jin finally found out about her husband's affair and the location where he was living with Wu. Unable to bear it any longer, she went to catch them in the act at midnight on the 21st of this month, dragging her husband and Wu to the French police station to file a lawsuit, requesting investigation and punishment. The police station detained Yang and Wu and escorted them to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court the next day. Because the Police Department requested a postponement of the investigation, it was ordered that the two defendants each pay a 500-yuan bail and be available for questioning at any time. This has already been reported in this newspaper. According to the Second Special District Court, this is the first case of a wife catching her husband in adultery since the new criminal law took effect on July 1st. Article 239 of the criminal law on offenses against marriage and family states that "a person who has a spouse and commits adultery with another shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to one year. The adulterer shall be punished in the same manner." This case was continued yesterday morning at 10:00 AM in the Eighth Criminal Court by Judge Chen Pusheng and Clerk Shen Jikui of the Second Special District Court. The defendants Yang Gengquan and Wu Xuezhen were not present. Lawyer Yao Zhaodi of the Police Department stated the results of the police station's investigation and prosecuted them for adultery. The plaintiff Yang Jin also arrived in court, submitting a petition to withdraw the lawsuit. The judge then questioned Jin, asking if she really wanted to withdraw the lawsuit. She nodded in affirmation. The court verified the statement and immediately ruled that the public prosecution in this case was not accepted. According to Article 239 of the criminal law, adultery is a case that can only be prosecuted upon accusation. The plaintiff can withdraw her lawsuit before the conclusion of the first instance debate. It is also known that the plaintiff in this case, Yang Jin, and the first defendant in this case, Yang Gengquan, have already had their relatives and friends mediate, and the two parties have agreed to divorce, allowing each to remarry freely. They have already signed a divorce agreement. Therefore, Yang Jin withdrew the lawsuit, and this amusing story of a wife catching her husband in adultery came to an end.

Robbery at Caonitang in Pudong; Robbery Case Also Committed on Changping Road; Transferred from Public Concession 124

On the 9th of this month, the home of Wu Yu in Yangjing Town, Pudong, was suddenly invaded by many robbers armed with weapons, who robbed clothes and decorations. Before leaving, they shot and killed Wu Yu. Upon hearing the alarm, the Public Security Bureau in charge began investigating and successively arrested nine suspects in Pudong: Liu Decai, Liu Xiaosizi, Ma Acai, Xu Zhiquan, Ding Er, Liu Shanping, Jiang Zhenhai, Cao Shanwen, and Xu Genbao. A Dimeng brand handgun and five bullets were found in a shed in Caonitang and taken back to the Public Security Bureau for detention. However, this news was discovered by the Gordon Road Police Station of the Public Concession, because Liu Decai and the others had also committed robbery and other crimes within the concession. Therefore, the Chinese detective Zhang Liang and a Western detective were dispatched to the Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday to negotiate, and they were allowed to transfer the nine people and the guns and bullets to the police station for detention. They were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Police Lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the case and requested permission for detention for investigation. According to Lawyer Zhang, the defendants in this case were arrested for robbery and homicide in Pudong, and the police station requested their transfer from the Public Security Bureau. After investigation, it was learned that they were also related to the Changping Road robbery case. It turned out that at 8:00 PM on the 6th of this month, the home of a Liang family resident at No. 27, Lane 88, Changping Road, was suddenly invaded by many robbers armed with weapons, who asked if this was the home of a Liang. At that time, Liang was outside enjoying the cool air. Seeing the situation, he knew they were not good people and shouted loudly. The robbers panicked. Moreover, the Liang family was not wealthy, so they only robbed three quilts. Just as they were about to flee, Wang Chengbin, a neighbor at No. 25, heard the alarm and opened the door to look. The robbers, fearing that he would be detrimental to them, took preemptive action and fired two shots at him. One bullet hit Wang's left leg, causing him to fall to the ground injured. The robbers then fled with the stolen goods. Wang was sent to Shilong Hospital, where Dr. Feng confirmed that his left leg bone was broken, so he is still hospitalized for treatment. After the incident, the police went to investigate and found two bullet casings in Wang's home, which they took for investigation. Now, the police have sent the handgun found in the possession of the defendants to the Shanghai Municipal Council Firearms Inspection Office. The results of the inspection confirm that it is the same handgun used to shoot Wang Chengbin on Changping Road, and the bullet casings are the same. As the investigation procedures are not yet complete, a detention is requested. Furthermore, Western Detective Ya Kelai of the Shanghai Municipal Council Firearms Inspection Office testified about the handgun inspection, presenting photos of the bullet casings. After Judge Liu Yugui briefly questioned Liu Decai and others, he ordered them to be detained for seven days for further questioning.

After the death of Guo Zibin, a wealthy Chaozhou merchant in Shanghai, his eldest son, Guo Huatang, filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against his stepmother, Guo Fang, and his younger brother, Guo Futin, for breach of trust and theft, claiming that they had used his seal to withdraw a large sum of money from the Xinyu Qianzhuang. Central Bank Inspection Report 126

The 245th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes states: "In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the number of convertible notes issued by this bank and its reserves. The 245th inspection was held in the Issuance Bureau of this bank on August 24, 1935. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of silver yuan convertible notes issued is 10,928,1278 yuan, including 10,226,1508 yuan in silver yuan notes and 7,019,770 yuan in subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 10,928,1278 yuan, including 8,438,1278 yuan in cash reserves. The cash reserves are stored in the issuing vault of this bank (79,277,230 yuan), branch banks in various ports (2,085,681 yuan), and with other banks (3,018,367 yuan). The security reserve is equivalent to 24,900,000 yuan. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.7 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserves is 373,324.7 yuan. The reserves include 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, equivalent to 373,324.7 yuan in customs gold at a fixed price of 5.0779. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the rest must be a legally qualified guarantee reserve. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This is hereby reported. August 26, 1935. Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank: Li Fuxun, Supervisors: Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilun."

Sports News

Sixth National Games Announcement: Women's Outdoor Base Ball Rules, Competition Summary 135

Women's base ball is a game played by two teams, each with nine players, playing seven innings each. When one team is at bat, the other team fields. This alternates, with each team batting once, which constitutes one inning. The batting team's players should try to become runners, circling each base and returning to home base to score points. The fielding team's main goal is to prevent the opposing team from occupying bases and scoring. After all innings are completed, the scores of both teams are calculated, and the team with the higher score wins.

Article 1: Equipment

A. Field

Size of each side of the field, pitching distance, diagonal distance:

(1) 35 feet, 30 feet, 49.5 feet

(2) 45 feet, 35 feet, 63 feet

(3) 60 feet, ×36 feet, 84.8 feet

(4) 65 feet, 40 feet, 92 feet

×For younger female players, the pitching distance for a 60-foot field can be changed to 33 feet.

(Note): The Sixth National Games will temporarily use a 35-foot field, but the ball used will have a circumference of 12 inches.

Section 2: Home Base. Home base is made of white rubber or painted wood, in a pentagonal shape, firmly buried in the ground, with its surface level with the ground. The two sides of its pointed end match the angles of the first and third base lines, each 12 inches long. The two sides of the flat end run parallel to the straight line between home base and second base, each 8.5 inches long. The flat end connecting these two sides, which is the front of home base, should be 17 inches long.

Section 3: First, Second, and Third Bases. These three bases are all made of 15-inch square white canvas bags, filled with soft materials such as sawdust and yellow sand. Each base should be placed at each corner of the field, with its two sides aligned with the base lines.

Section 4: Pitching Plate. The pitching plate is a rectangular board, 24 inches long and 6 inches wide, buried level with the ground. The ground within the field can be sloped with the pitching plate as the center, but the height of the plate must not exceed 10 inches above each base line or home base.

Section 5: Batting Area. There are two batting areas, located on the left and right sides of home base, each forming a rectangle of 5 feet long and 3 feet wide. The longest side runs parallel to the diagonal line between home base and second base. If the lead line at the 12-inch point of the home base's pointed end is taken as the standard, then 2 feet of the batting area is in front of this line (i.e., inside the field), and 3 feet is behind it. The distance between the two rectangles is 29 inches, and each inner side is 6 inches from home base.

Section 6: Boundary Lines. The base lines between home base and first base, and between home base and third base, extend from each base to the boundary of the field, and are called boundary lines.

Section 7: Coaching Lines. Coaching lines run parallel to the lines between home base and second base, and between home base and third base, each 6 feet outside the base lines, starting from the intersection of the base lines and extending towards home base, to a length of 15 feet.

B. Ball

The ball should be an official playground ball, with three circumferences: 14 inches, 12 inches, and 9 inches, depending on the size of the field (see Article 1, Section A, Table). The weight of the 12-inch ball should be between 5 and three-quarters ounces and 6 and a half ounces.

C. Bat

The bat is round, with the diameter at its thickest point not exceeding 2.5 inches, and its length not exceeding 34 inches. There are no restrictions on the bat's weight or the type of wood used.

D. Player Equipment

If using a 65-foot field, fielders may use gloves.

(Note): According to the Rules Committee, catchers should use masks and chest protectors.

Article 2: Game Terminology

Section 1: Obstruction. If a batted or thrown ball is touched, obstructed, or caught by someone not participating in the game, it is called "obstruction."

Section 2: Coach. A player listed in the batting order who stands within the coaching line's range when their team is at bat, providing guidance to their teammates who are running bases, is called a "coach."

Section 3: Fielder. Any member of the fielding team participating in the game on the field is called a "fielder."

Section 4: Fly Ball. A ball that is caught before it touches the ground after being hit is called a "fly ball."

Section 5: Forced Out. A "forced out" occurs when a batter becomes a runner, and a runner already on base is forced to advance to the next base, losing their right to continue occupying that base, and is therefore out.

Section 6: Inning. An "inning" refers to the instance when a team is at bat until three of its players are out.

Section 7: Infield. The area of the field within the four base lines is called the "infield."

Section 8: Outfield. All of the field outside the base lines, between the boundary lines, and within the field's edge is called the "outfield."

Section 9: Wild Throw. A ball thrown to a fielder that is too high or off to the side, and the fielder fails to catch it, is called a "wild throw."

Section 10: Passed Ball. A legally pitched ball that is not touched by the bat, and the catcher fails to catch or control it, is called a "passed ball."

Section 11: Play. "Play" is the command given by the umpire to officially start or resume the game after a timeout.

Section 12: Time. "Time" is the command given by the umpire to stop the game before it starts.

Article 3: Officials and Their Authority

A. Officials

Section 1: The officials for a formal game should include: (1) one or two umpires, with two being preferable, selected by both competing teams simultaneously. (Note): The National Games will hire the umpires. (2) Two scorekeepers.

B. Authority of the Umpires

Section 1: Head Umpire. If there are two umpires, one should be the head umpire, responsible for the entire conduct of the game, positioned behind the catcher. Their duties are: (1) To accept the batting order submitted by both team captains before the game starts. (2) To announce which team bats first, and the names of both catchers and pitchers before the game starts. (3) To command the formal start of the game. After a timeout, the same "play" command is used to continue the game. (4) To announce "time" when there is a legitimate obstruction during the game. (5) To announce "end" when the game is over. (6) To resolve and judge all actions related to the pitcher, catcher, and batter. (7) To rule on the outcome of runners at home base. If all other bases are occupied, the same ruling should be made for third base. (8) To notify the scorekeepers and the opposing team of player substitutions and position changes based on the team captain's report. (9) To obtain the opposing team captain's consent if one team requests a runner substitution. (10) To declare a forfeit. (11) To suspend the game. (12) To disqualify a player for improper behavior, if necessary.

Section 2: Base Umpire. If there are two umpires, the other umpire is called the base umpire, positioned at any location most convenient for executing the ruling. Their duties are as follows: (1) To rule on the outcome of runners at first, second, and third base (except when the head umpire is designated to make the ruling according to the rules). (2) To assist the head umpire when necessary.

Section 3: If there are two umpires, they should not argue about rulings or interfere with each other, but should offer their opinions when the head umpire requests assistance.

Section 4: Single Umpire. If there is only one umpire, this umpire is responsible for the entire conduct of the game, positioned at the most convenient location for executing the ruling, and possesses all the authority of both the head umpire and the base umpire.

C. Duties of the Scorekeepers

Section 1: There should be two scorekeepers during the game, each appointed by one of the competing teams. One is called the scorekeeper, and the other is called the checker. The visiting team has the right to appoint the scorekeeper. The duties of the scorekeepers are as follows: (1) The scorekeeper is responsible for filling out the scorebook, and the checker is responsible for reviewing the records from the side. (2) If there is a dispute in the record, the head umpire should be notified immediately, and they should make the most appropriate decision based on their knowledge, and may also request the base umpire to participate if necessary. (3) To accept and record the batting order of the players submitted by both team captains before the start of the game. (4) To notify the umpire immediately if a team does not follow the batting order. (5) To record player substitutions and position changes based on the umpire's notification.

Article 4: Teams

A. Players

Section 1: Number of Players. Each team should have nine players present for a formal game at any given time, one of whom is the captain. However, with the consent of both team captains, this can be changed to ten players. (Note): The Sixth National Games stipulates that each women's base ball team should have nine participating players.

Section 2: Player Positions. Each team should consist of a catcher, pitcher, first baseman, second baseman, third baseman, shortstop, right fielder, centerfielder, and left fielder. If ten players are used, there will be two shortstops, named left shortstop and right shortstop.

Section 3: Player Positioning. Players should stand in any location within the boundary lines designated by the captain, according to their position, except that the pitcher must stand on the pitching plate before pitching (see Article 7, Section A, Paragraph 1) (Refer to Figure 2).

B. Player Substitution

Section 1: Except when the ball is in play, substitutes can enter the field at any time to replace players in the batting order. However, players who have been substituted out are not allowed to re-enter the game.

Section 2: A runner cannot be replaced by a teammate listed or not listed in the batting order before reaching first base, and the substitution must first obtain the consent of team captain A.

Section 3: Players can change positions on the field at any time, but the captain must report the change to the umpire, and their batting order should remain the same as before the change.

Section 4: If a team captain does not participate in the game, they should designate one player from their team at the batter's bench to perform their duties.

C. Responsibilities of the Captain

Section 1: The captain is the representative of a team. Their duties are as follows: (1) To participate in the draw to determine selection rights. The winner of the draw gets to choose whether their team bats first or takes the field as the fielding team. (2) To report the batting order of the team to the scorekeepers and umpires before the start of the game. (3) To designate the positions of the team's players on the field. (4) To agree with the opposing team captain in advance if the formal number of innings is not followed. (5) To respond after a decision if the opposing team captain requests to increase the number of players beyond the stipulated number (see Article 4, Section A, Paragraph 1). (6) To report player substitutions and position changes to the umpire as soon as known. (7) To accept or reject the opposing team captain's request to substitute a runner who has reached first base. (8) To request the umpire to interpret the rules when necessary, but not to dispute the accuracy of the umpire's observations and rulings.

National Arts Disaster Relief Performance News: Second Preparatory Meeting Last Night 142

The Shanghai National Arts Association and the Jingwu Athletic Association, two martial arts groups, believe that the floods in various places are extremely severe and the situation is very tragic, and that funds should be raised for relief. Educational News

Qingdao City: Universal Compulsory Education Plan, Stipulating Compulsory Enrollment Measures, Total Annual Funding of 85,000 Yuan 143

Qingdao Correspondence: The Municipal Education Bureau, following orders to implement universal compulsory education, has drafted a "Twenty-Fourth Year Implementation Plan for Promoting Compulsory Education." This plan has been submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. The total annual funding is 85,000 yuan. The bureau's proposed universal compulsory education plan and compulsory enrollment measures are detailed below:

Universal Compulsory Education Plan

The "Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education in the City in the Twenty-Fourth Year" had previously been drafted and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record. The points listed in that plan were based on the principles and regulations for promoting compulsory education in the city. Now, with the budget finalized and all surveys completed, a detailed plan has been formulated as a basis for implementation. However, there are two differences between this plan and the previously submitted one: 1. The number of classes added has been reduced. The previous plan proposed 350 classes, while this plan specifies 311 classes. 2. The total funding has been slightly reduced. The previous plan proposed over 96,000 yuan, but the actual allocation in this plan is only 85,000 yuan. The bureau's original submission anticipated an annual subsidy of over 48,000 yuan from the Ministry of Education, with the same amount raised locally. Therefore, the original plan could add up to 350 classes. However, the ministry's approved subsidy for this year is 22,000 yuan, which is over 16,000 yuan less than expected. It is extremely difficult to raise additional funds locally, so it is necessary to reduce the number of classes to balance the budget. The actual amount of funds raised locally is over 53,000 yuan, which is over 5,000 yuan more than the original amount (48,000 yuan). The total funding, including the Ministry of Education subsidy and local funds, is 85,000 yuan. It is planned to allocate 55,000 yuan for the expenses of opening and reforming classes, 16,000 yuan for construction costs, and 14,000 yuan for initial equipment costs. According to actual calculations, it is possible to add or reform classes to include 24 regular classes, 40 new two-shift classes, and 178 reformed two-shift classes. Education in this city has always been considered widespread, with schools in all rural areas. The best way to implement universal compulsory education is to utilize existing school buildings and classes to operate two-shift classes. However, because classrooms in all schools are already full of students and there are no spare rooms for students in the two shifts to share, it is proposed to adopt a half-day two-shift system for ease of management and instruction. If schools can find a way to adopt a full-day teaching schedule, they can apply to do so. The duration of study in the two-shift classes is tentatively set at two years, equivalent to the level of the first two years of elementary school. School-age children who complete two years of study will be issued a certificate of completion of compulsory education. If they wish to continue their studies, they can still enter the third grade. Implementing the program in this way can utilize existing schools to popularize compulsory education and preserve regular elementary schools, so that universal compulsory education will not come at the expense of regular elementary schools, thereby affecting the level of education. B. Compulsory Education Funding: 1. Sources of Funding: (1) 53,000 yuan from the Municipal Government's treasury; (2) 32,000 yuan in subsidies from the Ministry of Education; totaling 85,000 yuan. 2. Allocation of Funding: (1) 16,000 yuan in subsidies for school building construction; (2) 14,000 yuan for start-up costs; (3) 55,000 yuan for the annual operating expenses of establishing new schools, adding classes, and reforming existing classes. 3. Standards for the allocation of operating expenses: (1) The funding for adding regular senior classes to municipal, township, and district elementary schools will be handled according to the existing standards, i.e., one and a half teachers will be added for each senior class, with a monthly salary of 34 yuan. One and a quarter teachers will be added for each junior class, with a monthly salary of 31 yuan. Office expenses will be determined based on the number of classes, ranging from six to nine yuan per class. (2) One teacher will be added for each two-shift class in municipal elementary schools, with a monthly salary of 34 yuan. Office expenses will be calculated according to standards. (3) One teacher will be added for every two two-shift classes in township elementary schools, with a monthly salary of 31 yuan and office expenses of 5 yuan. (4) For each two-shift class reformed in township elementary schools, the salary of teachers in full elementary schools or branch schools will be increased by three yuan. If it is in a junior elementary school, one teacher will be added for each reformed class, with a monthly salary of 28 yuan. (5) For schools established in newly designated districts, the monthly salary of the principal of a full elementary school will be 36 yuan, the principal of a junior elementary school will be 33 yuan, senior teachers will receive 31 yuan, junior teachers will receive 28 yuan, and office expenses will be 5 yuan per class. (6) Each newly established school and each newly added class will be given two months of winter coal expenses, at 9 yuan per month.

Compulsory Enrollment Measures

(1) These measures are formulated in accordance with Chapter 2 of the "Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Outline of the Provisional Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education" of the Central Ministry of Education. (2) All school-age children (from seven to thirteen years old) in the city's area must enroll in school to complete their compulsory national education. (3) The number of school-age children in the city's area will be investigated once a year in June by the Education Bureau in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau, under the supervision of the Municipal and Township District Offices and school police stations, as the basis for compulsory enrollment. 4. After the investigation is completed, each office will prepare statistics on school-age children in its district and submit them to the Education Bureau and the Public Security Bureau for record-keeping. The original registers will be kept in the office for future reference. 5. The period before the start of the spring and autumn semesters of elementary schools each year will be the period for compulsory enrollment. In addition to schools recruiting students on their own and filling vacancies, if there are insufficient places, the school should report to the district office, which will investigate the school-age children's register, select those who are older and from wealthier families, compile a list, and have the office send it to the district's Public Security Bureau to urge them to enroll. 6. If all school-age children who are older and from wealthier families have been enrolled, and there are still insufficient places, they should be filled with children from poor families. The office will also compile a list and send it to the Public Security Bureau to strictly urge them to enroll. 7. For children who have been urged to enroll by the Public Security Bureau, the principal will report to the nearby police station and give their parents a verbal warning. If they still do not enroll after two days of warning, the principal should report to the office, which will impose a fine of between one and five yuan. 8. The above fines will be handled by the office. The fine notice will be forwarded to the Public Security Bureau for delivery to the police station for enforcement. 9. The police station should enforce the collection of fines within six hours after the fine notice is delivered. Even if the parents verbally agree to pay or rush to send their children to school, they will still be fined. Those who refuse to pay the fine may be temporarily detained. 10. The receipt for the fine will be prepared by the Education Bureau in triplicate with an official seal and sent to the Public Security Bureau for distribution and use. 11. The triplicate receipt for the fine will have the first copy for record-keeping, the second copy for verification, and the third copy as a receipt, which will be issued to the fined household after the fine is paid in full. 12. At the end of each month, the police station will verify the second copy of the fine receipt and send it to the branch station, which will submit it to the Public Security Bureau for forwarding to the office to verify the amount of the fine. The office will then issue a list and send it to the Education Bureau for safekeeping. The first copy of the record will remain with the police station. 13. The fine money will be used by the Education Bureau for the benefit of the school to which the fined household belongs, in the following ways: (1) To enrich equipment, (2) To subsidize the cost of books for poor students. 14. The parents who have been fined must still send their children to school within three days. If they still do not comply, they may be fined twice the amount of the first fine, and the above procedures will still be followed. 15. If a school-age child drops out of school for no reason or is absent for more than one week, and repeated requests for them to return to school are ignored, the principal may report to the office, which may impose a fine of between one and five yuan and still order them to return to school. 16. If a student withdraws from school due to a family move within the city, the school must verify the new address, report it to the police station, and the police station will notify the police station in that area to urge them to enroll. 17. If a school-age child has an epidemic or other reason and cannot attend school for a while, their parents or guardians may submit a written request for exemption from school. Those with chronic illnesses or idiocy who are incapable of receiving education may have their parents or guardians request exemption from school. All applications for delayed schooling or exemption from schooling must be approved by the office to be valid. Each office must also submit a separate report. 19. The term of the first phase of compulsory education in the city is tentatively set at two years, using a two-shift teaching system. Students who have completed two years of education will have the school apply to the Education Bureau for a certificate of short-term compulsory education. Continued education is permitted. 20. During the first two phases of compulsory education implementation, if school-age children have been educated in private schools or at home and pass the assessment of the local elementary school, they will be given a certificate of short-term compulsory education. If they do not pass, they must still enroll in school. 21. These measures may be amended at any time if there are any omissions. 22. These measures will be implemented from the date of submission and approval.

According to the institute's first-class regulations, the top five students with outstanding performance, who have missed less than one-tenth of the classes, will have all their tuition fees refunded. Therefore, those students who have not missed classes have been working even harder recently, hoping to get their tuition fees refunded. It is reported that the committee has submitted an application to the Ministry of Education to continue running the second class, and registration begins today. The Popularity of the "New Standard Singing Textbook" Published by Kaiming Bookstore 149

The "New Standard Singing Textbook for Junior High School," compiled by music education experts Qian Juntiao and Wang Xiang, and published by Kaiming Bookstore, was published in its entirety in mid-July, divided into three volumes for the three academic years of junior high school. Its compilation generally follows the new standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education and incorporates more than ten years of teaching experience. The content is very precise, and the combination of exercises and songs is especially rare in similar books. Famous figures in the music world have unanimously praised it as the best textbook. Schools adopting it have flocked to it. The first edition sold out in a few days and has now been reprinted. Each volume is priced at six jiao and sold at an 80% discount.

Little Men (27) 151

—Original work by Ms. Louisa May Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

Chapter 3: The Path of Light

When Ned walked into the classroom on Monday morning, he was not without fear in his heart, because he was deeply afraid of exposing his stupidity to the public. However, Mr. Pei deliberately placed him in a seat deep in the recess by the window, with his back to the others, and sent Fang Lang to guide him in his studies, so no one else would hear his mistakes or see the mess of ink on his writing book. He was truly grateful for this situation and worked very hard. Later, Mr. Pei saw his hot face and black fingers and said with a smile:

"Don't work too hard, my child; if you're afraid of getting tired, you can do it a little more leisurely."

"But I have to work hard, otherwise I won't be able to catch up with others. They know a lot of things, and I don't know anything," Ned said, truly falling into a state of despair. Hearing the other children answer questions about history, geography, and grammar, he felt that they were extremely familiar.

"But you also know many things that they don't know," Mr. Pei said, sitting next to him, as Fang Lang had gone to lead a group of young students through the maze of the tax law's multiplication table. "Really?" Ned looked, seeming unable to believe what Mr. Pei had just said.

"Really; first of all, you can control your temper, while those who excel at solving mathematical problems often cannot; this is a very important lesson, and I think you have already learned it well. Secondly, you can play the violin, but none of the children here can, even though they all long to. But the best thing, Ned, is that you really want to learn something. With that, it's as if you're already halfway there. It may seem difficult at first, and you may feel discouraged, but just keep doing it, and then you will naturally find that everything gradually becomes easier."

Foreign Banks Reduce Activity, Standard Gold Price also Rises by 1.8 Yuan; Daily Market Conditions Shift from Firm to Flat, Demand and Supply are Unsatisfactory, and Fluctuations are Narrow

Yesterday's gold market saw foreign banks reducing activity and prices initially trending upward. Unexpectedly, the central bank's listed price did not change, and the standard gold price instead decreased. Buyers took advantage of this momentum to actively sell, causing prices to fall again. However, the daily market was extremely flat, and the final result was a slight improvement. Exchange rates were slightly higher. London spot gold decreased by two pence. In off-exchange pre-market trading, prices opened and immediately rose to above 80 yuan. Foreign Exchange: Apparently Flat, Actually Tight; Foreign Banks and Sassoon Buying and Selling; Golden Gang, Bank of Communications, and Zhejiang Industrial Bank 154

Yesterday's foreign exchange market was affected by overseas news from London, with near-term contracts reduced by 3125, and far-term contracts reduced by 25. The New York silver market was reduced by 125, and Montry forward silver prices fell by 1.5% to 4%. London spot gold fell by two pence. The pound rose against the dollar by 75, the dollar rose against the pound by 125, the pound rose against the franc by 3 points, and the dollar rose against the franc by 25. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with recent selling prices: 1 shilling and 6 pence for the pound, and 37.25 yuan for the dollar, compared to last Saturday, the pound was tighter by 0.0625 and the dollar was tighter by 0.125. After opening, the market was flat. Then, the Central Bank's listed prices were announced, and both the pound and the dollar were flat. Customs gold units were reduced by four cents, and confidence was slightly weak, leading to a slight easing. Although the Japanese Bank Mitsui was selling, Dai-ichi Bank was buying. Banks traded with each other, and the situation was still flat. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's listed prices were announced, and both the pound and the dollar were flat. However, due to the tendency of Chinese merchants to sell, it was difficult to rally. The Hong Kong market was initially tight and then loose after opening, but the fluctuations were extremely small. Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 172

— (Zhu Weixuan)

Summer night fireflies, because they emit shimmering light, invite the playful minds of children, leading to their demise. Therefore, when engaging in society, one must not be ambitious and reveal too much brilliance, or the result will be the same as the firefly's!

In the wind and rain, on the boundless sea, occasionally two or three small birds flit by. Seeing their weary and powerless state, yet their unavoidable flight, is akin to a person's lack of diligent striving in life, resulting in a fall into the abyss and drowning!

A hen fighting a wildcat, a puppy challenging a tiger, though they possess the will to fight, will quickly die! Therefore, if one does not possess sufficient strength, never strike a stone with an egg and invite destruction!

Memories of Sacrificing to Confucius 173

— Li Qing

Since the fifteenth year of the Republic, the grand ceremony of sacrificing to Confucius has long been abolished. Last year, the National Government designated August 27th, Confucius' birthday, as a National Memorial Day, ordering all agencies and organizations to take a holiday for commemoration and to hold solemn memorial ceremonies. Although the rituals differ from the past, they evoked my early memories of participating in the sacrifices to Confucius, which I write about haphazardly for the reader.

The Liyan Academy in Jiangyin was originally connected to the Wenmiao (Confucius Temple). Since the Xinhai Revolution, the academy was converted into a school, and the buildings were separated. I studied at Liyan in the past and was twice selected as a dancer. According to the ritual, sacrifices to Confucius required seventy-two dancers and twenty-four musicians, collectively known as the "music and dance performers." The musicians, under the direction of experienced individuals, sang verses from the Book of Great Harmony, while the dancers, holding shields in their left hands and halberds in their right hands, advanced, retreated, knelt, and prostrated themselves, which Confucius would appreciate.

We rose at midnight, ate the thin rice porridge prepared in the school, then donned green silk ceremonial robes similar to Daoist robes and square scholar hats. We marched in formation to the Wenmiao, prepared to participate in the ceremony. The ceremony was scheduled for 2:00 AM, but the chief officiant was often a lazy opium addict, and by the time he arrived at the temple, it was usually dawn. During that prolonged time, we wandered around, admiring the display of the "tailao" (full offering of ox, sheep, pig) and "shaolao" (smaller offering) on large platters. I wondered why Confucius and his disciples insisted on eating whole oxen and sheep, leaving people with a crude impression.

Once the sacrificial ritual began, experts like literati leisurely struck various ancient bronze blocks. Although it was ancient music, the sound resembled the "cacophony of clay pots" as described, and those with some musical knowledge could not sense its beauty. As for the carving of patterns on some bronze blocks, they did possess artistic merit.

Everyone participating in the ceremony received compensation. For the music and dance performers, there were two legs of beef and one sheep. The musicians received twenty-four steamed buns, and the dancers received sixteen steamed buns. Besides the beef and sheep given directly, the steamed buns were distributed in the form of tickets. Each ticket was for four buns, and the ticket holder could exchange it at the designated steamed bun shop. However, for students with "face," being selected was perhaps worse than not being selected, because after being selected, one had to give one or two tickets to friends who were not selected. One could, at most, enjoy three tickets, i.e., twelve buns. Those not selected, on the other hand, could obtain seven or eight tickets by begging and asking, exceeding the dancers' share by one hundred percent. These people who gained without labor, of course, were limited to the special class of students.

Little Western Paradise 174

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Episode 18: Qi Party High-Climbing Fawning Rebukes Petty Official, Fierce Female Prowess Arises, Noisiness Annoys Lady

He called the tea boy and said sternly: Secretary-General Qiu, who came with Commissioner Lan this time, is a relative of mine. Here's a letter, you must deliver it to him. Speaking, he handed the letter to the tea boy, and at the same time took a copper ticket worth twenty copper coins and gave it to him, smiling: This is for you to buy a pack of cigarettes. But there's one thing, you must deliver this letter to Secretary-General Qiu's hand. He's a very modest person and doesn't want people to call him Secretary-General, just call him Secretary. Secretary doesn't sound very good, so just call him Mr. Qiu. Isn't that what they call those high-ranking central officials, Mr.? The tea boy smiled faintly, threw the copper ticket on the table, and said: I have cigarettes to smoke, I don't need your money. Saying that, he took the letter and walked out. Zhang Jiefu chased him outside, shouting: This letter is very important, you must deliver it to Mr. Qiu's hand. That tea boy did not turn his head back, and kept walking forward with the letter. Jiefu stood blankly on the corridor, very regretful, thinking in his heart, if he gave him ten cents, he might be happy. Now that he had been generous, he should have been generous to the end, but now saving twenty or thirty copper coins, he was afraid it would hinder his business. Just as he was thinking so, Li Shilian came out of the room from afar and bowed deeply to Jiefu. He smiled and said: Congratulations, congratulations. Jiefu was thinking about things, and was suddenly congratulated by him, but he was a little confused, widened his eyes, and kept looking at him. Li Shilian smiled and said: That Commissioner Lan is here, you can find a position, isn't this a happy event? (300)

Tofu Xi Shi (Tofu Beauty) 175

— Zhang Muliang

In the Hongkou area, as long as you mention the name "Tofu Xi Shi," everyone, young and old, knows who you're talking about.

Tofu Xi Shi's real name is unknown, but it's known that her family runs a tofu shop. Because she has a very likable face, people gave her this elegant nickname. She has studied the art of dealing with people in daily life very well. In front of old ladies, she speaks of the boundless Buddhist Dharma; in front of old men, she laments the hardships of the world; such handling of people makes people feel very comfortable. Moreover, her nimble mouth always addresses people with such endearing terms as "Uncle," "Elder Brother," "Auntie," "Good Granny"...!

But recently, Tofu Xi Shi has started to dress up in flamboyant ways, learning to be beautiful, and she has also put on airs when dealing with people.

Whenever she dresses up and goes out, those nosy neighbors will tease her, saying, "Oh dear! The fashionable elder sister is here!" But as soon as she hears such teasing, she puts on a widow-like face, acting as if something important has happened, and ignores you. Because of this, people began to suspect that she might be up to something outside.

About a few months later, it was said that Tofu Xi Shi no longer dressed up flamboyantly to go out, and stayed at home all day long.

"Alas! What a beautiful young girl has died!" The good granny next door to Tofu Xi Shi came to tell people.

Later, everyone understood that she had died from an abortion, a very tragic ending that made them only lament for her!

So in the Hongkou area, no one heard her beautiful name anymore!

Voices from the Powder Box 176

— Jiang Mi

Records of Lingering Fragrance 177

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

So I tried to explain the materials, usage, and preparation of French hair dye to her to the best of my limited knowledge. However, my own knowledge of cosmetics was too little and I couldn't explain it clearly to her. She was very understanding, and dropped the subject after hearing it. However, I was clear on the effects of hair dye, so I was able to explain that point clearly to her. As a result, I persuaded her very hard.

"I'll write to France to order it," I finally said, "and then have them send the medicine from France. It will take at least forty or fifty days for the whole process. Is the Empress Dowager okay with the wait?"

"Not late, not late, forty or fifty days are just a fleeting moment in a person's life," the Empress Dowager replied seemingly patiently. "If you think this dye has special effects, we are willing to try it."

The matter was decided like this. I was truly indescribably happy that the Empress Dowager had allowed me to help her. After leaving, I rushed to find an eunuch to go to my house to tell my father, asking him to immediately send a telegram to Paris, asking a familiar friend to buy some of the best hair dyes for us and send them quickly.
