Biographical Sketches

Mrs. Chevalier's Skillful Husband Management 178

— Haike

French film star Maurice Chevalier, who starred in Hollywood's "The Merry Widow," "Midnight in Paris," and "The Passionate Plumber," gained popularity worldwide, especially among women, for his romantic and humorous style, earning him the title of "World's Greatest Lover."

British magazine reporter Ms. Li specially visited Chevalier's wife, asking her for her opinion on her husband being admired by women. Mrs. Chevalier replied with the following words:

"I am very happy to see my husband so popular. It is to be expected that he would win the love of many women. This is also part of his work.

"How can one find happiness with jealousy in one's heart? Jealousy and happiness cannot go hand in hand. Of course, I understand that women love my husband because I love him that way, too.

"I think if you love your husband, you should bring a maternal aspect to your love. For example, if you are a loving mother, you cannot be selfish. You must see your son happy often.

"In today's world, many people's lives are full of unhappiness. If my husband can bring them some joy, that would be the best thing. I will never forget that others do not have my good fortune.

"Moreover, if husband and wife can trust each other, then they will not want to make the other unhappy. If a woman is often suspicious and jealous, then the man will think, 'What's the use? I might as well do bad things.' Isn't that what I said?

"If a wife can give her husband a happy life, forgetting all worries and troubles, then the husband will naturally be happy to stay with her.

"A man always seeks someone who can comfort him and spend his free time with him. He wants to be comfortable and forget everything. He hopes his wife will be with him, giving him sweet comfort. Aren't these things easy for women to do? So if his wife cannot give them to him, he will naturally go to others.

"Husband and wife cannot both be leaders. I think it's more natural to let the husband take some authority, because he is more suitable for it than women.

"But that doesn't mean women should submit. If she has the skill to manage her husband, can't she be the master?

I think one must work constantly at marriage to achieve perfection, so when I married my husband, I was willing to abandon my career. I felt that if I continued my life as a singer and dancer, I could not create a good home for him. I put all my time into the duties of the home, and I thought it was very important.

"I know my husband respects my duties at home, just as I do for him. Both sides do their duty, and there is no difference between important and unimportant, but the two of us, one is conspicuous in front of the crowd, and the other is conspicuous in the rear. But the rear is as important as the front.

"When I had to abandon my hard-earned career at first, I felt reluctant, because I would no longer be the famous Feng Na Fan Li on the stage, but began to be Mrs. Chevalier. But you can believe now that I am happy to do so, but nothing is more satisfying than being loved by a good man and having a happy family life. Women need these things above all fame and praise.

"When my husband is starring in a film, he works very hard, so I have to find a way to protect him from some harassment, so that he can focus on his work. You must understand that I always want to make him worry-free.

"He is very responsible for his work and is never satisfied with his past achievements. Often when a film is finished, he is already worrying about preparing for the next one.

"So when my husband comes back, I always try to make him forget everything in the studio. We only talk about many interesting things. He talks and laughs, and his heart relaxes. But sometimes he has difficulties in his work and wants to discuss his plans, so I listen quietly. I don't express any opinions, because he knows more than I do after all! I just encourage him and make him happy. This is very important for any man. The next day, he can cheer up and go out to continue his work. All wives should keep this firmly in mind.

"Of course! My husband also has some temper, otherwise, he would not be a great artist. But he doesn't throw tantrums for no reason like other artists. When he gets angry, I walk away and leave him alone. Isn't that the best way?"

Free Talk

Style and Imitation 179

— Yi Feng

In the literary styles currently popular, we often hear people say that so-and-so has the style of Turgenev, so-and-so is rich in Gorky's style, and so-and-so is close to so-and-so. Such comparisons are truly commonplace and not at all strange.

Such comparisons are incredibly harmful to contemporary writers, overshadowing the supreme crown they wear.

A writer who is willing to bury his head in his writing efforts may initially, intentionally or unintentionally, imitate the styles of others. Over time, his work may inadvertently become tainted by the influence of so-and-so. This is a common occurrence. However, we cannot say that he has succeeded in becoming so-and-so, or even a reincarnation of so-and-so. This is also very clear. Because no matter how much imitation occurs, the author will never be without his own presence in his work. If he has himself, then how much has he learned to resemble? What kind of self is he? Questions arise everywhere. If this self is filled with ignorance and stubbornness, or if what he imitates is ultimately an antique or fossil, then such an author and such a work are fundamentally soulless corpses, rotten objects covered in mold.

Fortunately, even if what he imitates succeeds in achieving a certain percentage of someone else, and that person's model is suitable for the current style, but his own ambition and development are not compatible with it, then what is this someone who has learned to be successful at a certain percentage worth!

Kharatkevich explained this most clearly. In "How I Wrote Cement," he wrote:

"I don't ask myself: how would Tolstoy, Turgenev, Dostoevsky, or Gorky write this, say that. I never even thought about these questions; even if I did, I would banish them, because it is not only unnecessary but also harmful; otherwise, I would be attached to the model and lose my freedom to create."

From this, we can see how a literary giant succeeded in his greatness. Is it self-creation or just imitation?

Let him continue:

"Inheriting art includes the determination to overcome the styles of previous generations, and this is to complete one's own style...

"The difficulty lies not in how to use existing artistic methods (nothing is easier than imitation), but in how to create one's own unique methods, proving to be a new stage of beauty in artistic thought."

This is even clearer, explaining how a writer should be steadfast in his writing and establish his own unique style.

Young writers should also humbly learn from open-minded senior writers in many ways, but not imitate them. It is not a bad thing for a writer to unintentionally accept the influence of someone in his cultivation, but it is unacceptable to resort to imitation. This tendency should not be allowed to develop for long, let alone become deliberately imitative.

Therefore, the aforementioned "commonplace" comparisons create not a new style for great writers, but only arrogance and more deliberate imitation for contemporary writers.

On a Yangtze River Steamer (II) 180

— Ye Zi

The woman let out a sharp cry, rolled over, and her limbs immediately stretched out, stiffening on the ground!

"You dare to ride our foreigners' boat without a ticket, you rotten X!…" he rushed forward, adding curses, as if he were a foreigner himself.

The mother was anxious! She pushed out to grab the pockmarked man, afraid that he would kick her again; at the same time, she protested and questioned:

"Why did you hit her? So fierce!… Didn't you see that she's pregnant?"

"You dare to ride our foreigners' boat without paying?" The pockmarked man retorted with a red face, while eyeing his accountant's face.

"Then, it's just—money…………"

"Hmm! Money!…" another tea boy added heavily.

The mother pondered for a moment, unable to think of a solution, and the woman groaned loudly on the ground! A portion of the onlookers immediately began to discuss in alarm and urgency. But the tea boy with the stick raised the stick high, attempting to continue striking.

The mother rushed to block the tea boy; and approached the woman, looking at her belly with great pity. Suddenly, she stopped groaning, shrinking into a ball with convulsions, her eyes bulging, her teeth tightly biting her lower lip, and screaming in stomach pain! The mother panicked, bent over, squatted down, and stroked her stomach slowly, in waves. Moreover, out of excessive anger, she scolded the brutal tea boy loudly, shouting out the dangerous signs of imminent birth!

The onlookers all retreated. The accountant spat harshly in disgust and hurried away. The tea boys, unable to gain ground, followed like dogs, cursing back with filthy words, and retreated into their cabin.

I also turned to leave, but the mother called me back: instructing me to immediately go to my berth to tear off the yellow blanket; and borrow a pair of scissors and a thin hemp rope.

I went. Hastily passing through the curious, gossiping crowd, when I returned with the items, the mother had already undressed the woman's lower body. A large puddle of filthy water flowed on the ground. Her lips were bitten bloody by her teeth, beads of sweat popped out on her forehead, and her whole body struggled painfully and with difficulty! As soon as she saw me, she turned her face away in shame and shook her hands wildly! But, in an instant, a tiny red baby, dripping with bloody filth, squeezed out! It fell on the ground, crying out its unknowable fate!

I quickly turned away. The mother panted laboriously for about five or six minutes before finally extracting a bloody placenta and throwing it from my left side into the depths of the river.

"It's completely beaten down!" The mother said to me, raising a pair of blood-stained hands in anger: "They are all vicious robbers!… That fetus is simply too small to live. And they are still waiting to ask her for the fare!"

"Then what to do?"

"Saving people requires saving them completely!…" The mother said in a resolute, police-like tone. "Go get me a cup of water, let me wash the child first and then think of a way…"

The sun had already climbed more than ten feet high from the mountains on the left bank of the river. The river wind was gentle, completely losing its nocturnal fury. From the distant tip of the right bank of the river, the outline of the tail of a big city slowly crawled over.

Artist 181

— Hu Kao

Journey 182

— Especially

Wearing the stars,

Swallowing the mountain wind of the quiet night,

Dark and faint in the distance—

Those are the peaks, those are the thickets.

It is the waning moon time,

Clear, the Milky Way cuts through the long sky,

Open your eyes wide, count them—

Hum, how can you count them clearly?

Tread lightly, I hear this mountain is not clean,

Let's drop another pair of straw sandals!

Crawling, not daring to make a sound,

Rushing on our journey.

The small temple in the corner of the mountain is making noise,

Pinching cold sweat, quietly slipping past,

Potholes, bumps, disregarding everything,

Dot by dot, are hidden lanterns!

Love (4) 183

— By S. Ersegev. Jinski, translated by Su Ming

The river grew wider, carrying him along high banks covered in forest, sometimes between many cliffs. He still had to watch ahead, so as not to crash into the large rocks in the water. Shavaka’s semi-savage eyes could see most of the living things in the water and on the shore. In Siberia, summer is not long. In August, the nights were already cold, and he needed a coat. By early September, he could see ice floes in the water, and suddenly one day, snow began to fall instead of rain, and a storm hit him.

Shavaka planned to spend the winter in a village he passed, but while he was still far from any village, the river had already frozen over. Shavaka dragged his boat to a place on the shore, where he saw a cave high on the bank, its entrance half-covered by a large pine tree blown down by a storm. The branches of the pine tree could be climbed up and down like a ladder, and the cave was originally as big as a room. Shavaka brought everything from the boat into the cave, and then happily went to cut some fuel. He used stones to block the entrance of the cave, leaving only a small crack; from the sparse pine branches, he made himself a door; he set up a place to make a fire, and used his axe to open a hole for the smoke to escape. When he first sat down in his cave, and his kettle began to boil in a warm and comfortable room instead of in the open air, he felt completely satisfied with his success, and fell asleep on his pine branch bed.

Waking up, he went to see if his boat was safe. Snow was falling densely, and everything was silent. The whole river was silent, covered with new, solid ice overnight. Shavaka said loudly, "Oh, friend, where have you come to! It doesn't matter, this place is good. There's nothing to shout about." In his long solitude, he had learned to talk to himself. He used words that were so simple and stingy, just as if he were talking to someone else.

When the ice was frozen solid, he used an axe to chisel a hole for the first rope, and then another for the second, and then he set up his net. Thus, in this place that he had never known before, and even now, he still knew nothing about, he began to spend his lonely winter.

Remembering Ming Ruo 184

— By Mu Shiying

The night rain pattered on the window glass. Facing the quiet gauze lamp on the desk, I thought of some old things and some old people.

It was two years ago, also on a night with rustling autumn rain, that Ming Ruo and I spent a long, long night in a small city's inn. It was a very old inn. Lying in bed, you could hear the mice running wildly on the ceiling, the hushed whispers of a prostitute and a foreign cloth merchant next door, and the raindrops, just like tonight, steadily beating against the window. The night in a small city is so quiet that there are only the sounds of dogs barking and the watchman's clapper. Listening to the weeping night rain, after lying in bed for a while, I finally sat up again and started smoking, gazing at the dim oil lamp. Ming Ruo didn't seem to be asleep either. Seeing me sit up, he turned over and asked:

"Can't sleep?"

"The rain in the small city is really unbearable, really unbearable."

"Wouldn't it be nice to talk, listening to this tireless rain?"

"But in Shanghai, the rain softens and hazes the neon lights. Ming Ruo, do you remember those Saturday nights we wandered in the streets in the rain?"

He seemed to be thinking about something, sighing and saying, "Look, isn't it fast, so fast? Those days have passed so quickly! You are still a young man sparkling with vitality, but I am already a clod of gray earth. Shanghai, haven't we left Shanghai for a year already?"

His face was blank and looked very depressed. This surprised me. Ming Ruo had always been a bright, humorous, and understanding person; among friends, he had the nickname "Essay." He was a typical small-city resident, who liked to enjoy trivial pleasures in life. After preparing his lessons, he often went to the small restaurant at the school gate to order a few cups of cocoa, eating peanuts and chatting with me about everything under the sun, saying some harmless jokes. He never got angry, nor excited, and as for depression, he didn't seem to have such emotions. That day, unexpectedly, he put on such a depressed face. Maybe it was because of the sad drizzle in this deep night? But after a while, he cheered up again and said:

"If the rain doesn't stop tomorrow, let's play mahjong all day. Imagine, taking off our socks, smoking little cigars, rolling up our sleeves, drawing an inlaid eight-s initially, and then drawing a 'bian san wan' on the second round! He was saying that, and he laughed happily.

"But I have to go back tomorrow no matter what."

"Stay another day. Do you think it's easy to meet up? After leaving school, today is the first day we've met up. Life is like duckweed, who knows when we'll be able to talk half the night like today again."

"If it rains, I'll stay another day."

But the next morning, when we woke up, we saw a very clear sky as if washed by rain. That day, I finally left. When I left, he saw me off at the station and told me to write more letters. Things rarely go as you wish, and even everyday things like writing letters are not entirely under the control of the will. After returning to Shanghai, I only wrote two letters in a year. He also seemed to not have much spare time, and his letters were not frequent either. Because of the infrequent letters, we finally stopped writing to each other.

Last October, he suddenly sent an invitation and a letter, telling me that he was about to get married, and wrote the following very simple and sincere words in the letter:

"A string of Yuanming chrysanthemums has bloomed by our fence. It's been two years since we parted. No matter how busy you are, come and see an old friend, see the clear countryside, see your old friend's lover, and be our groomsman."

I rushed around for several days, preparing to go to his hometown, a small town on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line, Chang'an, to see an old friend and enjoy a few days of leisure. But life is very cruel, and I still couldn't go this time. After that, he didn't send a single letter, and I only got some not very detailed news about him from others.

This spring, I met Brother Jia Bi, and he told me:

"Do you know? Sheng Ming Ruo is gone."

Dead? I didn't quite believe it. We were all very young people, and Ming Ruo had just gotten married and was a fellow with a good soul. Did he die so easily?

Recently, Brother Qian Gongxia came from Ming Ruo's hometown. When I asked him about Ming Ruo, he said:

"Dead, this spring."

Really dead, this good person! Just as he said, fast, so fast, those days passed so quickly. Those days... those days—and now he is already lying underground, and I have already become a clod of gray earth!

Thunderstorm 185

— By Ouyang Shan

Our friend Liu Li, who was like a mountain, told us many stories. He himself liked the scenes and characters he described more than anyone else, and his face, made of black English stone, would shine with a compelling light. One of them described a thunderstorm.

"...One autumn evening, I was walking from Hengjiao Village to Mian Village—I knew this road well, so I didn't bring a flashlight. The sky was originally very calm, and I didn't expect it to rain, but it did. It was very heavy. The mud on the road was washed away in less than ten minutes. The coarse sand and small stones bared their long, sharp teeth, biting many holes in my bare feet, causing them to bleed." Liu Li imitated the movements of that time, and began like this.

"I've never encountered such a heavy rain in my life—and such angry thunder! In the darkness, there was nothing but the rain and its sound. But just think: when lightning strikes, you see a world... trembling before your eyes, and the rain actually seems to disappear. When there's thunder, you can't hear the rain.

"I went to an old goose farmer's house to take shelter. His name was Bai Maolao, he was lonely, tall, and had a long white beard. As soon as I pushed open the door and entered his shrine, he loudly stopped me. He didn't pour me tea or bring out dry clothes... He took down two bamboo-woven rain hats from the wall, and lectured me like an elder: 'Is this the age to be avoiding rain? Come with me to the goose shed, I'm going to check on those little things.—Don't go in, you'll startle them. You have things you can look at yourself. Do you like to see the patterns of lightning and the sparks of thunder? Very good, for decades, that's been my hobby! Don't be afraid of it.'

"In front of the goose shed, I did as he told me. I stuck my head out from the night broken by the rain. I straightened my spine as straight as a coconut palm. The spray stung my eyes and nostrils. This time, instead of stealing a glance, I really saw lightning and thunder for the first time!

"I had a rain hat, but it didn't block me at all. I can't describe it anymore, I can only feel it! How a huge, twisting, rapid sword dazzlingly illuminated my eyes and the eyes of all the mountains, rivers, and jungles; how angrily, ruthlessly, and wantonly it tore open the swollen belly of the sky! How the fellow wielding the sword roared and howled! His voice was a heavy iron block, incomparably heavy, accompanied by a crisp, solid burst of sound when it rubbed against sparks, falling onto the mountains, tombs, plains, and rivers, shaking the entire earth, and then exhaling groaning echoes... continuing, not stopping for what felt like an immeasurable amount of time.

"That sword might suddenly stab next to you. Nothing to be afraid of, this is no longer a time to be afraid... You will feel yourself suddenly shrinking, without internal organs, brains, thoughts, memories, you feel like you only have a small piece of wood left, that is yourself. Next to you is an infinitely high wall, composed only of light.

'Nothing to be afraid of, friend, it's a very beautiful sky scene.'"

Female Gonorrhea 190

— Doctor Liu Xuannv

Female gonorrhea is completely the same as male gonorrhea. It is caused by infection with gonococcus. Others are caused by infection with bacilli, staphylococcus, streptococcus, or a mixture of various bacteria. After infection with this disease, it goes through a certain incubation period, the mucus phase, the inflammation phase, and then the purulent discharge phase, discharging a large amount of pus. When the lesion is only limited to the urethra, there are no subjective symptoms, only a slight feeling of moisture near the urethral opening, slightly different from usual. However, the female urethra is short and wide, so after infection with this disease, it is easy to develop bladder inflammation. Cystitis often develops after urethritis. After cystitis develops, the patient's subjective changes are significant, such as frequent urination. Sometimes, because the body cannot be kept still, it can immediately spread to the entire surface of the bladder. At this time, the most obvious symptom is painful urination several times an hour, with hematuria. However, mild cases only feel itchy and may have subsequent inguinal lymphadenitis. These acute symptoms are often alleviated with ordinary treatment. However, if the bacteria penetrate deeply and become chronic, it is more difficult to treat than in men. Most women are ashamed to seek medical treatment because of this hidden disease. They do not know that the harm is endless and they will regret it later. The best way to treat the disease is to seek medical treatment while strictly adhering to health preservation. However, sometimes due to time and space constraints, or the burden of family and economy, one can only seek self-treatment. Among the self-treatment methods, the best is to use both oral and external methods. Talk

From "Children's Year" to "Children's" Theater 192

— A Traveler in Gangnam

This year is a year of many disasters. War, floods, droughts... compounded by frequent foreign troubles. It is truly more tragic than any other year. It seems not too much to call it an unprecedented year of disaster. However, unexpectedly, from August 1st of this year, it was designated as "Children's Year." In such a year of many disasters, to be able to pay special attention to the lives of children, it seems like something to celebrate for our large group of children.

Now that "Children's Year" has begun, people are busy celebrating "Children's Year" and are committed to "working hard" for children's culture and various undertakings. Among them, the most "hardworking" are a group of merchants. They make sanitary candies for children, create new-style clothing and toys for children, and publish a large number of children's books. Even film merchants who have never paid attention to children are preparing to produce a large number of children's films from this year onwards. This grand and mighty array is indeed enough to make children happy. It's just a pity that these blessings can only be enjoyed by some wealthy children. The homeless street children still only quench their thirst with plums, unable to share any of it. Therefore, I think that if we really want to designate a "Children's Year," then we must designate a "Street Children's Year" for street children, because after all, the status of the two types of children is too different to be mixed together. The kind of street children in Pantaleev's "Watch" who can get such a good education opportunity cannot be found in China at all.

But I have to say again, China's special environment is somewhat different from other countries. Although we cannot say, like fatalists, that we have to wait for many years before we can immediately achieve this stage, it is indeed true. What's more, our country is still trapped in a year of many disasters in the midst of deep water and scorching fire?

After reading Pantaleev's "Watch," quite a few people expressed some opinions such as sentiments. Some people are even afraid that we will imitate blindly, so when they hear someone clamoring to adapt this fairy tale into a movie, they can't help but have some objections, and as a result, no one continues to adapt it. In fact, there is no need to worry about this. I think that if the screenwriter has a bit of vision, he will definitely clearly see the current situation in China, and adapt (adapt!) based on the "Chinese situation," at least it is no longer completely the same! Moreover, I think the significance of adapting "Watch" is more practical than someone adapting "Education of Love," because what is said here is not fantasy, but fact.

Therefore, I think of the street children who love drama in general. Their dramas are very simple and relevant to their lives. They love puppet shows, shadow plays, big plays... Sometimes, they simply use their own torn clothes, short bamboo poles, etc., a few people get together, and start acting. Perhaps they didn't think about whether this was for fun or for what, but they are the same as ordinary children in their love of drama. It's just that they don't have the money to go to the theater to watch plays, to go to school to act in plays, but only watch street plays on the street, and play the nondescript "children's plays."

Everyone seems to agree that drama and film contain educational significance. Then, I think, now that the production of children's films is being enthusiastically promoted, children's theater seems to be a matter that cannot be ignored, right? Moreover, I think that using street theater to educate street children in general is more interesting than forcing them to join literacy classes. Even for ordinary, more "fortunate" children, training them to become a group of children's theater actors, and providing them with some simple and meaningful plays to watch, is as necessary as giving them movies to watch.

Pine Forest 193

— Yago

After passing the Seven-Foot Ridge and going down the slope, I suddenly heard someone shouting behind me: "Hey! Friend, wait a moment." I stopped and looked back, only to find that it was an old man selling raspberry, carrying a heavy load and braving the scorching sun of July, panting as he rushed down from the ridge. I waited silently for him to arrive, and then started walking again.

He pulled a towel from his shoulder, wiped the sweat off his face, followed closely behind me, and muttered worriedly:

"This kind of weather... Someone will get heatstroke... Haven't seen it in thirty years."

I ignored him, rushing on my way, calculating the distance I had traveled in my mind.

After the Lesser and Greater Heat seasons, the weather has been extremely hot, and the sun is like a fiery wheel patrolling in the sky.

The old man selling raspberries ran as if he were crawling. After a while, when I turned my head to look, he had unconsciously fallen far behind. He anxiously and suffocatingly shouted loudly in a pitiful tone:

"Hey! Good friend, for the sake of an old man, wait for me one more time!" I had to stop the load again, hid under a willow tree by the roadside and waited for him. He limped with his short legs and crawled over, also put down the load. This time he was afraid that I would rush on my way immediately, making him unable to keep up and being left scattered on the remote mountain ridge, so he said:

"In such sultry weather, you have to stop and rest for a while, don't be in such a hurry, anyway, you can't make it to the early market."

I thought his words made sense, so I agreed to rest, but I said:

"The willow shade here is not good for resting, let's go to the pine forest ahead!"

He hesitated at first, but later agreed. We picked up the loads and walked slowly. He was very excited, no longer as sullen as before, and loudly ridiculed the unreasonable hot weather, the low price of raspberries, the difficult life of the poor, and so on. I occasionally interjected one or two sentences from his words, agreeing or explaining his words. He was extremely excited and exclaimed loudly behind me:

"The young people of this generation, I say, all have problems. There are few who are as sensible and reasonable as you."

We talked and walked, and unknowingly arrived at the pine forest at the foot of the hill. We chose a place where we could sit down and rest, put down the loads, took off the bamboo hats from our heads and fanned ourselves. The old man chose a pine root to sit on, and asked me to sit opposite him, took out a pipe from his waist, filled it with tobacco, and smoked leisurely. After a pipe, his spirit became more lively and excited, and he said loudly for no reason:

"Good friend, do you know the story of this pine forest?" I shook my head, and he laughed. "It's like this. Three years ago, in a June when raspberries were on the market, I sold a load of red raspberries from Sicheng and hired a porter to carry them through here. It was a sultry day, and the sun was burning like fire. After rushing down the ridge, we were both too hot to walk, so we rested in this pine forest. You think, we hadn't rested for even the time it takes to eat a meal when a miserable whimper came from the pine forest. We didn't know why, but the more we listened, the more frightened we became. The porter was so scared that his face turned pale and his mouth turned white, and he trembled and shouted, 'It's bitter!' and fainted. I was so scared that I didn't know what to do, so I ran away, running towards a place where there were people.

"I ran desperately, and I don't know how long I ran before I stopped in a village. Thinking of that load of raspberries, I shouted for help. The villagers quickly ran out and surrounded me. I told them everything. Everyone was very surprised at the time, and about a hundred people were gathered, carrying knives and guns, and went straight to the pine forest. My red raspberries and the porter were gone together. I couldn't help but cry out in pain. Everyone comforted me and said, 'It must be inside!' So we went into the forest, and after running through countless twists and turns, someone found bloodstains on the ground. Running further in, there was a whole small leg of a woman, hanging bloodily on the tree. At the same time, someone heard a faint cry. This scare made everyone unable to take care of everything and ran around.

"Since then, it has been rumored that there are living demons appearing here. People are afraid and dare not pass through here again. The reason I asked you to wait just now was because I was afraid of being alone. Now that we have two companions, what are we afraid of!"

After the old man finished telling his story, he had enough of his tobacco addiction, and said excitedly, "Let's go!" Everyone started walking again.

Father and Son 194

— Xiao Qi

Uncle Sanxi, who went out naked twenty years ago, returned naked a month or two ago after twenty years. It's like a dream. Half a lifetime has passed in the blink of an eye. Uncle Sanxi is now approaching fifty years old, but he doesn't have the decadent look of an old man. His eyes are still very sharp, and he can still walk long distances in the hot sun. His body is so fat... What can it be compared to except a plump sow. Now it is the end of midsummer, and fat people are very afraid of heat. Uncle Sanxi is especially afraid. His whole body is layered with folds of flesh. Every day as soon as the sun shows its face, he runs out to blow the wind under a pile of big banyan trees outside the house, wildly waving a fan, but sweat still hangs down in large clusters like a sudden rain. So Uncle Sanxi only wears a pair of shorts from morning to night, his upper body completely naked, his big belly protruding, but he still shouts and yells, unbearably hot. So he must take three or five well water baths a day...

Uncle Sanxi has been away from his hometown for a full twenty years, and as a result, he has become a pauper, which is enough to make his family deeply disappointed. In addition, he has brought back an even more abhorrent bad habit - drinking. He must have a glass of wine with two of his three meals a day, otherwise he simply can't eat. But his alcohol tolerance is not high, and his temper is bad. After drinking two or three glasses of wine, his face immediately turns red, and he staggers, one step at a time, from the store to home, and from home to the store, or he just sits on the doorstep of his house, opens his sandy and sluggish throat, and rambles in front of everyone:

—Achang doesn't look at me, does he still recognize me as his father?

In a drunken daze, he always particularly complained about his son Achang, and even cursed at him. He is old, and he is somewhat taking advantage of his drunken outburst. No one argues with him, no one answers him, letting him babble endlessly. Everyone advises him to go back to the house and have a good sleep, and not to get angry and catch a cold. Sometimes he hasn't finished his own words when he can't support himself and falls to the ground from the threshold with a "thud," and waits for his son to help him back to the house. Others don't have the strength to care about his heavy body, they just stand and watch. Every time it often ends with such a funny scene.

Uncle Sanxi often quarrels with his son Achang. Father and son can't get along. His family of six or seven people all rely on Achang's small fruit shop in the nearby street to support them, but the market is bad, and the money earned is limited. The days are almost dragging on day by day. After Erxi returned, he helped look after his son's shop, but he didn't understand how to work at all, he only knew how to drink and spend his days idly. As for the burden of the family, because Achang was shouldering it, he didn't think about it at all, and he was free and comfortable. At first, his son sent him to the fruit market in the morning with money to buy some fresh goods. But once he went, a journey that could be returned in an hour, he often didn't return slowly until noon, with red eyes and speaking incoherently, the strong smell of alcohol rushing out of his mouth in waves. Naturally, it was clear at a glance that he had deducted the money for buying goods to drink alcohol, and the same situation happened several times. Achang couldn't help but get angry, but he just looked at you without any expression. After that, Achang didn't dare to trust his father anymore, so he had to run errands himself, and then asked Sanxi to guard the shop. But as soon as Achang went out, Sanxi had his way again. He secretly reached into the big bamboo tube with copper coins and grabbed a handful, hiding it in his pocket. Later, he let an ignorant grandson guard the shop, and he quietly slipped out. Soon Achang came back, and as soon as he saw the scene, he immediately understood clearly in his heart. However, he could only frown. As an old man, he still doesn't know whether he's dead or alive, there's no way, so he sighed.

After this, Achang had to manage the money in the shop strictly himself. When he was not in the shop, he asked his wife to manage it, so that it was impossible for Sanxi to get a single copper. Therefore, Sanxi occasionally drank alcohol and took the opportunity to scold his son.

New Chapter of the Flood 195

— (By Mr. Hu Zhimei)

Floods reaching the sky have been heard since ancient times. King Yu controlled the floods for nine years and succeeded. This year is. Along the Yangtze River and the Yellow River. The raging waves break the banks and harm the people. The vast overflow is difficult to contain. I don't know how many thousands of people have drowned. Houses collapse. Fields and crops are submerged. Everyone's property is gone. People and animals drift with the waves. A vast expanse of water is level with the roofs. The most tragic. Half asleep in the middle of the night, dreams are not stable. In an instant, wind and waves bring great disaster. The wind is like hitting. The waves are like rushing. Raindrops are like soldiers on standby after sleeping. Oh. Pity. But hear. Calling children. Calling mother. Sad sounds mixed in the roaring tide. Even if you shout until your throat is hoarse. It is really difficult to pull you out of the city of wrongful death. A family's flesh and blood are all scattered. Where to find the living and the dead? Hungry in the stomach and left in the water. Even if you don't die, it's hard to escape. Such a disaster situation is so tragic. How many times have people heard of it? Think of you, living in a heavenly fairy Buddha land. Abundant food and clothing are too much, and you are also powerless. You must know. Disaster areas are not like dance floors. Embracing each other in the dusk. Drifting with the waves, the body has no master. Sad voice. Don't see that. Traffic lights. You must know. Disaster areas are not like movie theaters. Immersed in water, cold as ice. No need. To eat ice cream again. You must know. Disaster areas are not like parks. Murmuring and talking about love. Only hear. Crying and shouting for a savior. You must know. Disaster areas cannot be used as sea bathing. Neither has. Rubber ring. Also doesn't have. Lifeboat. Only that. A board. A bench. Seeking survival in the stormy waves. Comparing the bitterness and happiness in this way. Heaven and hell are clearly divided. I am. Singing to the point of sadness, my heart is tired. Tears are like broken strings of pearls. Also like. Ten thousand steel knives piercing the chest. Therefore, I still hope that you will be generous. Vigorously donate to help the disaster victims. Fortune and longevity, and many children and grandchildren.

Chen Juanjuan Learns to Drive a Car 201

The Beginning and End of the "Big Family" Story 202

Disaster All Starts with Family Division

A perfectly good rural family, owning a lot of land, with five brothers (eldest Wang Xianzhai, second eldest Xi Jianong, third Sun Min, fourth Gao Zhanfei, fifth Zhao Dan). They should have cooperated, inherited the family business, saved this bankrupt rural village, and lived a happy and peaceful life.

However, they ended up, because of suspicion between brothers and jealousy between sisters-in-law, dividing the good family into a mess. Family division is not absolutely a bad thing. It can promote independence and upward courage among individuals, but the eldest Wang Xianzhai and Yi Jue Lin both admired the city life. After the division, they moved to Shanghai, speculated unsuccessfully, and were deceived. Not only did they themselves taste the bitterness of family ruin, but they also implicated the second and third brothers, who also perished in the wave of urban sins.

"Nora" in the "Goddess of Freedom"

When Wang Xianzhai, Xi Jianong, and Sun Min were critically ill in the hospital one after another, Gao Zhanfei and Zhao Dan rushed to visit them. Wang Xianzhai, in broken sentences, spoke of his current awakening and regretted his past mistakes. The desolate and tragic emotion filled the surroundings of the sickbed, but regret was already too late. In an instant, they successively embarked on the road to death.

Finally, Gao Zhanfei shouted the slogan of returning to the countryside, and Zhao Dan also wanted to give up his studies and work with his brother in rural work.

Return to the countryside! This is the high-pitched cry in the "Big Family" because, although the countryside has already gone bankrupt, it is not a good business to squeeze into the economically collapsing metropolis.

Facing Death, Pure Regret for the Past 203

Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

Architecture in Amsterdam, Netherlands (Part 1) 205

— Yue Qi

Amsterdam in the Netherlands is one of the cities famous for its architectural art, and it is also a city with clear contrasting colors. It has monuments rich in historical interest; it also has equally interesting completely modern buildings related to modern business. In the crisscrossing canals, yachts painted in old-fashioned colors sail leisurely, while on the banks, noisy cars rush by. People walking on the streets mostly wear modern clothes, but everywhere you can still encounter pedestrians dressed like their ancestors.

Like many important cities in Northern Europe, Amsterdam's main activities are forever related to the shipbuilding industry and shipping business. Managing waterways is one of Amsterdam's biggest problems. The construction of dams and the cutting off of canals have made Amsterdam almost a group of small islands. These canals, no more than three and a half feet deep, are kept fresh by the irrigation waters of the North Sea River.

On both sides of the Grachts, which are connected to each other by small canals, are the houses of old merchants and important citizens. These noble houses are mostly Dutch style, completely different in nature from those in other parts of Europe. Their ages vary, but their structures are generally the same. Houses from the early seventeenth century stand next to houses from the eighteenth century and later. Both types of buildings are based on driving wooden piles into the mud, the difference being that early houses used more wood, while later houses used more cement.

The structure of the old merchants' houses on both sides of the Grachts is mostly wood-based. After the wooden piles are driven in, a wooden platform is built on top of the wooden piles, and a wooden framework is erected on top of the platform. After the framework is built, the walls are laid. The walls are painted with oil or tar to protect against moisture. Therefore, the old-fashioned houses in Amsterdam are mostly dark in color, but fortunately, the cheese-colored paint used on the wood and windows and the green paint used on the doors and windows mask the dark color a lot.

The interiors of these old-fashioned houses are quite interesting, and the layouts are almost the same. The basement is used as a kitchen and storage room. The door leading to the basement is located under the stairs leading to the main house. The lower floor of the main house is used as an office, and the upper floor is used as a residence. The floors and walls of the temple rooms are paved with dolomite; dolomite has a huge market in Amsterdam. Currently, these old-fashioned houses are almost entirely used for commercial purposes, and the houses from the early seventeenth century are used as warehouses, but the structure of these buildings still influences the design of modern architecture.

The restrictions and narrowness of the building site make interior design very difficult. One of the results is that the steps are steep, making it almost impossible to move heavy goods and furniture. Therefore, these houses are equipped with cranes to hoist goods. Cranes, which have become one of the characteristics of Amsterdam's architecture, are still used even in newly built residential areas; at the same time, in the recently built houses, these cranes have become indispensable, and the steep steps also exist as in the old-fashioned houses.

In the new areas as well as in the old areas, brick is the common material used for building houses. This is very natural in the Netherlands, because there are many good brickyards all over the Netherlands. The soil in these places creates bricks of various colors. Dutch bricks are completely different in size from bricks produced in other parts of Europe; the famous four-and-a-half-inch brick in England cannot be found in the Netherlands. Dutch bricks are rarely more than two and a quarter inches thick, and some are only one and a half inches thick. These small units give Dutch buildings a special character, especially when arranged in variegated colors. The same bricks are also used to build roads. The impression given is of completely brick-built streets, with houses and roads using the same materials.

The new construction in Amsterdam is very different in style from the old buildings, but they blend with the old buildings in a satisfactory way. All new buildings have a Dutch flavor that is entirely due to conscious or unconscious traditional forces. It is the spirit of this traditional force that maintains the special Dutch air that permeates Amsterdam.

Like most European cities, Amsterdam also suffered the fate of the advent of industrialism in the nineteenth century, at which time the situation in architecture was undifferentiated and unmanaged. The development of architecture did not follow rules; the construction of streets was not specially planned; several old and crowded areas in the east had almost become slums. Currently, the municipal authorities have planned to clear these eastern areas, and some residents have been relocated to new residential areas. Amsterdam's housing renovation plan began after World War I, when the motivation was a lack of housing. The municipal authorities adopted a policy of buying land at random opportunities to prevent land prices from soaring. Amsterdam's municipal renovation plan is very ambitious, but the steps to implement the plan are very steady. (To be continued)

Restrictions on Building Height 206

— Xu Pusheng

The construction of housing is closely related to human health, and whether or not there is sufficient sunlight is the most important factor. Housing needs sufficient sunlight and even direct sunlight. Mr. Charles B. Ball, the health director of Chicago, once said: If indoor light and air are not good, then physiologically, there will be a loss of appetite, weight loss, poor eyesight, and neurasthenia.

However, in modern times, with the development of commercial capital and the progress of building materials, such as the use of reinforced concrete, many towering buildings have been produced. The shadows of these buildings reduce the direct and indirect sunlight of nearby lower houses, thereby damaging the health of the residents. And for the buildings themselves, there are also disadvantages, such as the darkness in the lower-level rooms, which requires lighting even during the day; if there is a fire, then the danger for those living on the upper floors is even greater. Therefore, the cities of various countries have laws restricting the height of houses; the method is generally determined by the width of the road in front of the building. For example, the regulations in England and Japan are:

Japan Residential area—The height of the house shall not exceed one and a quarter times the width of the street in front.

Other—The height of the house shall not exceed one and a half times the width of the street in front.

England Residential area—One time

Other—One and a half times

If it is necessary to increase the height during construction, the building line must be appropriately set back, so that the street is widened, and in proportion, it still conforms to the principle of restriction, and the lower layers of the building and the adjacent houses can still receive the sunlight from the top of the opposite roof. However, the ratio of setback to height increase is also not uniform; if the setback is one foot, the number of feet to increase is at least half a foot and at most three or four feet, among which the ratio of one to one is the most common. However, some laws also limit this method; for example, in Japan, the maximum height of houses in residential areas must not exceed 65 feet, and in other areas, the limit is 100 feet.

Shanghai also has the same regulations on this matter:

The height of buildings along the highway shall not exceed one and a half times the width of the road. (That is, the ratio of the width of the road to the height of the building is 1 to 1.5) When the height exceeds the above regulations, the upper-level buildings should be retracted layer by layer in a ratio of 1 to 1.5. For buildings at corners, if the facades on both sides are equal along the road, the height can be based on the wider highway. The height of old-fashioned houses loaded with wooden pillars shall not exceed 11 meters (or 36 feet) and shall not be built on four floors. For houses with brick walls on all four corners, if the internal building materials are not sufficient for fire prevention, the height shall not exceed 18 meters (or 60 feet). The height of buildings constructed of steel, reinforced concrete, or specified fire-resistant materials shall not exceed 25 meters (or 82 feet). The height of the building is based on the road surface to the eaves. If there are additional buildings on the roof that exceed two-tenths of the total area of the building, then the height of the building should be based on these additional buildings.

Building towering buildings has no benefit other than saving land area; and the expenses incurred are doubled. The reason for this is nothing more than showing off to the public in order to achieve the effect of commercial advertising; therefore, these buildings are mostly department stores, not residential buildings. Since it is harmful to the health of the people, it should be restricted by law.

Tales of Architectural History (4) 207

— Bu Ren

However, although this method of construction seems almost permanently suitable for the British background, we now seem to have reached its end. This is because our way of life has changed so drastically and so rapidly in recent times. We modern people, due to the novelty of habits and the abundance of inventions, are not suitable for living in old-fashioned houses or entrusting ourselves to old-fashioned backgrounds. Moreover, the application of steel beams and reinforced concrete, as well as the methods of all new objects, require new designs and constructions, and then we can harvest satisfactory benefits.

At present, although there are still a few people who are still quite concerned about the magnificence of houses, most of us require lightness, ventilation, convenience, reasonable price, neatness, and smoothness for our residences. We do not need any decoration or pretense, we all need complete equipment provided by scientific capabilities that provide comfort, benefit, and labor-saving. Now, only a very small number of wealthy people love and have the ability to set up old-fashioned luxury buildings, and what most people need is pure architecture that has the three conditions of "sturdy," "practical," and "comfortable."

This of course refers to small and dense residences suitable for most people to live in. The apartment-style "high-rise" popular in Germany, Scandinavia, and the Soviet Union, and the skyscrapers of New York, are the products of this new trend. After having a small house that is enough to settle a family, we need more beautiful and spacious public houses to provide for public entertainment, education, and social purposes.

Because there are too many people who are dissatisfied with the old way of life, they will definitely start to experiment with new ways of life; at a certain period, the emergence of a certain type of building that suits the new way of life is undoubtedly. (End)

Various Valuations 208

— Xu Jiyao

The purpose of valuation is accuracy. Everyone can create the most accurate and convenient method and apply it. However, to know how to estimate accurately, you must first know how the common magic in the world is now, so that you can refer to it and improve it. Now I will describe the grain seed valuation method as follows:

(A) Cubic Foot Values. This estimation is widely used in European and American countries, that is, the entire volume of the building is calculated as a certain number of cubic feet or a certain number of cubic meters (all volumes from the bottom to the top of the roof). Multiply by the unit price per cubic foot or cubic meter to determine the cost of the building. This method calculates the area, height, depth, size of the foundation, and slope of the roof uniformly, so it is very accurate. The difficulty lies in the fact that the unit price per cubic foot or cubic meter must be accurate and there must be no difference between high and low from the actual value.

In all countries that use this type of estimation, their magazines contain the unit prices of various projects under construction (that is, the construction cost per cubic foot), so that all stakeholders know the value of various buildings and it is easy to compare and estimate the value of other types of projects to be built. (For example, if there is a project whose degree and grade should be similar to a certain project that has been completed, then its price should also be similar, so it can be estimated based on its unit price to calculate it. If there is a slight difference or the distance of transportation is different, then the unit can also be increased or decreased to estimate it.)

(B) Per Square Foot of Floor Space. Using the area of the building as the unit of estimation is also popular in Western countries. Now some people in our country also use this method. If the unit price used is not the appropriate amount, it is easy to cause extreme differences. Therefore, those who use this method to estimate in Beijing and Shanghai call it the general ledger, which is the account of the general situation, which can only be used as a quick estimation method but not a precise estimation method. Therefore, bidding and opening accounts must be opened separately to be based on and not to be excessive loss or gain.

This method only uses the floor area as the standard, regardless of the height of the house, the depth of the foundation, the slope of the roof, etc., so it is definitely not an accurate estimation. However, because it is quick and easy to understand, it is very suitable for engineers and owners to budget, because the engineer's budget has no profit or loss relationship, and the owner must submit the contractor's bid to determine its cost. The engineer's budget can only be used as a reference. Now those who use this method to estimate in Beijing and Shanghai take one British square as a unit, that is, one hundred square feet is one square. For example, a certain building has a floor area of ​​several squares, excluding the area of ​​the balcony, steps, platform, and other scattered works that cannot be included. If each square is a certain number of yuan, then the engineering cost of this building is equal to the unit price multiplied by the number of squares.

(C) The Quantity System of Estimating. This valuation is the most precise, that is, according to the drawings and specifications, the various projects in the building are calculated separately for their volume or quantity, and then the unit project price is estimated with reference to the specifications. After calculating its price item by item, it is then accumulated into the total project cost, so it is very accurate. However, before this type of valuation, the drawings of the building must be read repeatedly and the structure must be recorded in detail, and then the specifications must be consulted, and everything must be understood before each item can be estimated. Otherwise, there will be many omissions, which will easily lead to errors and cause losses. If you want to be precise but easy to make mistakes, it is better than the above three estimations. The easiest way to make this kind of price is to omit or repeat the separate calculations, which are often wrong or forgotten. If you want to avoid this disadvantage, you can also have two people make a paper of estimation and compare and correct it. In the Shanghai-Nanjing area, the method of opening detailed accounts is used in this method. We can understand from this account whether the detailed accounts opened by the contractor are calculated accurately, whether the unit price is appropriate, and whether the contractor understands the specifications in the drawings and specifications. Because this type of estimation cannot list the corresponding quantity and unit price if the drawings are not understood and the specifications have not been read. Generally, the detailed account is to separate each construction project into two parts, for example, the foundation, the number of squares of three-and-earth, the number of yuan per square, the number of squares of large feet, the number of squares of yuan per square, the 20-inch wall, 15-inch wall, and 10-inch wall are also listed separately as quantity and estimated. For example, one hall of the gate, how many double doors, how many single doors, and how many small doors are recorded separately and estimated one by one. Therefore, this type of valuation is the most time-consuming, often failing to complete an estimation in one day.

Combining the above three methods is the most common and practical now, but the old-fashioned valuation in our country is more precise than ever, because its estimation method is to calculate the number of wood roots, the number of brick materials, the number of tiles, the number of stones, the number of stone gray, the number of paper tendons, the number of carpenters, the number of workers, and the number of small workers, and the detailed listing is very precise. However, the results are also in line with those, so they often exceed the budget by a huge amount, or the too precise estimation is easy to cause errors, which is not as good as the above three estimations.
